2020.08.10 04.00 Bug fixes and correction to v03.00:

references
- Correcting YANG references for Non-Delay

- Correcting YANG references for enhanced U-Plane
markings

criteria which includes definitions in this
specification
- Clarification of supervision

- Enabling static configuration of PRACH or SRS
- Supporting flexible TDD pattern configuration
- To allow for different delay management
parameters for C and U-plane
- New sync capabilities for reporting estimated time
and frequency errors
- New capability to define compression on an
endpoint basis
- New optional feature – configurable full-scale
offset
- New optional feature - eAxC specific gain
correction
- New optional feature - TX gain reference level
control

DU

of O-RU resources

Chapter 1 Introductory Material 1
1.1 Scope 2
This Technical Specification has been produced by the O-RAN.org. 3
The contents of the present document are subject to continuing work within O-RAN WG4 and may change following formal 4
O-RAN approval. Should the O-RAN.org modify the contents of the present document, it will be re -released by O-RAN 5
Alliance with an identifying change of release date and an increase in version number as follows: 6
Release x.y.z 7
where: 8
x the first digit is incremented for all changes of substance, i.e. technical enhancements, corrections, updates, etc. (the 9
initial approved document will have x=01). 10
y the second digit is incremented when editorial only changes have been incorporated in the document. 11
z the third digit included only in working versions of the document indicating incremental changes during the editing 12
process. 13
The present document specifies the management plane protocols used over the fronthaul interface linking the O-RU (O-RAN 14
Radio Unit) with other management plane entities, that may include the O-DU (O-RAN Distributed Unit), the O-RAN defined 15
Service Management and Orchestration (SMO) functionality as well as other generic Network Management Systems (NMS).  16
1.2 References 17
The following documents contain provisions which, through reference in this text, constitute provisions of the present document. 18
- References are either specific (identified by date of publication, edition number, version number, etc.) or non-specific. 19
- For a specific reference, subsequent revisions do not apply. 20
- For a non-specific reference, the latest version applies. In the case of a reference to a 3GPP document (including a GSM 21
document), a non-specific reference implicitly refers to the latest version of that document in Release 15. 22

1.3 Definitions and Abbreviations 36
1.3.1 Definitions 37
For the purposes of the present document, the terms and definitions given in 3GPP TR 21.905 [1] and the following apply. A 38
term defined in the present document takes precedence over the definition of the same term, if any, in 3GPP TR 21.905 [1]. 39
Antenna Line: connection between O-RU and antenna 40
C-Plane: Control Plane: refers specifically to real-time control between O-DU and O-RU, and should not be confused with the 41
UE’s control plane 42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          12
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
Cascade mode: Mode of Shared cell which is realized by several O-RUs cascaded in chain topology 1
DL: DownLink: data flow towards the radiating antenna (generally on the LLS interface) 2
eAxC: extended Antenna-Carrier: a data flow for a single antenna (or spatial stream) for a single carrier in a single sector. 3
Event-Collector: A REST server to which an O -RU supporting NON -PERSISTENT-NETCONF feature can send a JSON 4
notification 5
FHM mode: Mode of Shared cell which is realized by FHM and several O-RUs in star topology.  6
LLS: Lower Layer Split: logical interface between  O-DU and O-RU when using a  lower layer (intra-PHY based) functional 7
split. 8
LLS-U: Lower Layer Split User-plane: logical interface between O-DU and O-RU when using a lower layer functional split. 9
LLS-C: Lower Layer Split Control-plane: logical interface between O-DU and O-RU when using a lower layer functional split. 10
LLS-S: Lower Layer Split Synchronization -plane: logical interface between O-DU and O-RU when using a lower layer 11
functional split. 12
High-PHY: those portions of the PHY processing on the O-DU side of the fronthaul interface, including FEC encode/decode, 13
scrambling, and modulation/demodulation. 14
Low-PHY: those portions of the PHY processing on the O-RU side of the fronthaul interface, including FFT/iFFT, digital 15
beamforming, and PRACH extraction and filtering. 16
M-Plane: Management Plane: refers to non-real-time management operations between the O-DU and the O-RU 17
North-node: the O-DU or a connected O-RU closer to the O-DU for the O-RU, e.g., the cascade O-RU#1 connected to O-18
RU#2 is north-node for O-RU#2, when O-DU, O-RU#1 and O-RU#2 are in cascade chain topology. The O-DU in star 19
topology connected to an FHM is north-node for the FHM.  20
NMS: A Network Management System dedicated to O-RU operations 21
Port: End of a transport link – in most cases this is an optical port 22
Port Number: A number which identifies a port (see Port). In case of SFP/SFP+ port, port numb er value is 0 to N-1 where N 23
is number of ports in the device. Numbers 0 to N-1 are assigned to ports in order following order of labels on the device (labels 24
for ports are not necessarily numbers starting from zero) 25
O-DU: O-RAN Distributed Unit: a logical node hosting PDCP/RLC/MAC/High-PHY layers based on a lower layer functional 26
split. 27
O-RU: O-RAN Radio Unit: a logical node hosting Low-PHY layer and RF processing based on a lower layer functional split.  28
This is similar to 3GPP’s “TRP” or “RRH” but more specific in including the Low-PHY layer (FFT/iFFT, PRACH extraction).   29
O-RU Controller: A network function that is permitted to control the configuration of an O-RU. Examples of O-RU controllers 30
include, an O-DU, a classical NMS, an O-RAN Service Management and Orchestration function, or other network automation 31
platforms.  32
S-Plane: Synchronization Plane: refers to traffic between the O-RU or O-DU to a synchronization controller which is generally 33
an IEEE-1588 Grand Master (however, Grand Master functionality may be embedded in the O-DU). 34
Shared cell: The operation for the same cell by several O-RUs.  35
Shared cell network: the network for several cascade O-RUs in a chain topology or the network for one FHM and several O-36
RUs in a star topology.  37
South-node: a connected O-RU far from O-DU for the O-RU, e.g., the cascade O-RU#2 connected to O-RU#1 is south-node 38
for O-RU#1, when O-DU, O-RU#1 and O-RU#2 are in cascade chain topology. The O-RU in star topology connected to an 39
FHM is south-node for the FHM. 40
Spatial stream: the data flow on the DL associated with precoded data (may be same as layers or different if there is expansion 41
in the precoding), and on UL associated with the number of outputs from the digital beamforming (sometimes called “beams”).  42
SSM: Synchronization Status Message: part of ITU G.781 and G.8264 standards. 43
TRX: Refers to the specific processing chain in an O-RU associated with D/A or A/D converters.  Due to digital beamforming 44
the number of TRXs may exceed the number of spatial streams, and due to analog beamforming the number of TRXs may be 45
lower than the number of antenna elements. 46

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          13
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
U-Plane: User Plane: refers to IQ sample data transferred between O-DU and O-RU 1
UL: Up-Link: data flow away from the radiating antenna (generally on the LLS interface) 2
Virtual Connection : a connection between O-RU and O-RU controller. This connection is established by means of 3
autodetection procedure and is supervised by supervision procedure. 4

1.4 Conventions 8
This management plane specification includes cross references to a set of associated YANG models. Text may reference 9
particular YANG leafs, notifications and remote procedure calls (RPCs). In order to assist in readability, all cross references to 10
YANG defined elements will keep the identical case format as defined in the corresponding YANG model, with the font-weight 11
set to bold. This convention applies only to text and not to YANG elements embedded into figures.  12
If there is any conflict between the YANG models and the accompanying text description in this specification, the definition of 13
the YANG models shall take precedence. 14
1.5 Topics for Future Specification Versions 15
Extensions to this version of the O-RAN WG4 Management Plane specification together with corrected errors will be included 16
in the future versions of this document.  17
 18
The following topics are to be considered for future versions of the specification: 19
1. Beam Id field interpretation for various types of beamforming 20
2. Redundancy and failover scenario 21
3. Shared cell support for IP-defined flows 22
4. Enhancements to better align with O-RAN Alliance O1 specification 23
 24
The revision statement in the YANG models will be used to describe future revisions to the models that are backwards 25
compatible. Backwards incompatible changes will be addressed by incrementing the number used as part of the model name 26
and namespace, effectively creating a new YANG model. The format of the namespace used in all O-RAN YANG models is 27
“urn:o-ran:”<model-name>“:”<model-number>, where the initial <model -number> used in a newly defined YANG model is 28
“1.0”. Where this document makes reference to m odels, irre spective of their backward compatibi lity, a gen eric <model -29
number> of “x.y” is used to enable reference to all versions of the namespace for a particular <model-name>. 30
 31
The revision statement in all YANG models includes a reference statement use d to cross-reference to the first version of this 32
document where the corresponding description was introduced . For example, the reference in all revision statements for the 33
initial O-RAN models include cross-reference to “ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v01.00”.  34
 35
The revision statement of the YANG models also includes a description which is used to track the versioning of the YANG 36
model. All revision statement descriptions will begin with “version ”<a>“.”<b>“.”<c>, where <a>, <b> and <c> are used to 37
reflect the version of the YANG model, where 38
 39

corresponding description was first introduced, corresponding to <x> in sub-section 1.1 41
<b>  is incremented when errors in the YANG model have been corrected 42
<c> is incremented only in working versions of the YANG model indicating incremental changes during the editing 43
process 44

Chapter 2 High Level Description 1
2.1 Top level functional description, terminology, including hybrid, 2
hierarchical 3
2.1.1 Architecture for O-RAN WG4 Fronthaul functional split 4
This O-RAN FH specification addresses the lower layer functional split as depicted in Figure 1. Refer to the O-RAN CUS plane 5
specification [2] for more details on the split architecture. The Lower-Layer Split M-plane (LLS-M) facilitates the initialization, 6
configuration and management of the O-RU to support the stated functional split. 7
 8
Figure 1 – O-RAN WG4 FH functional split 9
2.1.2 M-Plane architecture model 10
A NETCONF/YANG based M-Plane is used for supporting the management features including “start up” installation, software 11
management, configuration management, performance management, fault management and file management towards the O-12
RU. The M-Plane supports two architectural models: 13
1. Hierarchical model.  As shown on the left side Figure 1, the O-RU is managed entirely by one or more O-DU(s) using 14
a NETCONF based M-Plane interface. When the O-RU is managed by multiple O-DUs, it is typically for enabling O-DU 15
and/or transport connectivity redundancy capabilities. Refer to Chapter 3 for more details. 16
2. Hybrid model . As shown on the right side of Figure 1, the hybrid architecture enables one or more direct logical 17
interface(s) between management system (s) and O-RU in addition to a logical interface between O-DU and the O-RU. It 18
should be noted that the NETCONF clients connecting to the O-RU may be of different classes (e.g. O-DU and SMO). For 19
example, functions like O-RU software management, performance management, configuration management and fault 20
management can be managed directly by the management system(s).  21
In the hybrid model, the O-RU has end to end IP layer connectivity with the SMO. From a physical network point of view, this 22
connectivity could be via the O-DU, where the O-DU is acting as an IP/Ethernet packet forwarder, forwards the packets between 23
O-RU and the SMO. Direct logical communication between a n O-RU and SMO can be enabled via O-RUs being assigned 24

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          16
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
routable IPs or local private IPs resolved by a NAT function in the network (or implemented at the O-DU). Refer to chapter 3 1
for details how O-RU acquires the IP address of O-DU and SMO for the M-plane communication. 2
As described in Chapter 3, there is no expl icit signaling to indicate that an O-RU is operating in a hierarchical or hybrid 3
configuration. All NETCONF servers supporting this M -Plane specification shall support multiple NETCONF sessions, and 4
hence all complaint O-RUs shall be able to support both hierarchical and hybrid deployment. 5
 6
Figure 2 - M-Plane Architecture 7
NETCONF/YANG is used as the network element management protocol [3] and data modeling language [4]. Use of such a 8
standardized framework and common modeling language simplifies integration between O-DU and O-RU as well as operator 9
network integration (in terms of running service) in case of elements sharing a common set of capabilities . The framework 10
supports integration of products with differing capabilities enabled by well-defined published data models. NETCONF also 11
natively supports a hybrid architecture which enables multiple clients to subscribe and receive information originating at th e 12
NETCONF server in the O-RU. 13
2.1.3 Transport Network 14
Based on the transport topology, various modes of network connectivity are possible between O-RU and O-DU and SMO.  15
The basic requirement for M-Plane is to have end to end IP connectivity between the O-RU and the elements managing it (O-16
DU, SMO, or so called “O-RU Controllers”). The connectivity between the O-DU and SMO and its management plane are not 17
in scope of this specification. IPv4 shall be suppo rted as a mandatory transport protocol for M -Plane and IPv6 support is 18
optional.  19
2.1.4 M-Plane functional description 20
The M-Plane provides the following major functionalities to the O-RU. These features are implemented using the NETCONF 21
provided functions. 22

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          17
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 “Start up” installation  1
During startup, the O-RU acquires its network layer parameters either via static (pre -configured in the O-RU) or dynamically 2
via DHCP or DHCPv6. During this process the O-RU may acquire the IP address of the O-RU controller(s), in which case the 3
O-RU establishes the NETCONF connectivity using the “call home” feature. When the O-RU is operating in an environment 4
which include the O-RAN defined SMO, the O-RU may acquire the IP address of the event -collector(s), in which case the O-5
RU performs a pnfRegistration which triggers the SMO to establish NETCONF connectivity using the information recovered 6
from the pnfRegistration procedure.  The capability exchange is performed between the client and server as part of the initial 7
NETCONF Hello exchanges. Details of these steps are provided in chapter 3. 8
Note, the use of “start up” terminology in this specification is distinct from the “startup” capability used in a NETCONF 9
environment to indicate that a device supports separate running and startup configuration datastores. This specification makes 10
specific reference to configuration which is required to be stored in “reset persistent memory”. The O-RU shall use this stored 11
configuration as its “startup” configuration. 12
SW management  13
The M-Plane is responsible for software download, installation, validation and activation of new SW when requested by O-RU 14
Controller. The software download is triggered by NETCONF RPC procedures, and the actual software package download is 15
done using sFTP. In this version of the M-Plane specification, sFTP is the only defined file transfer protocol for software and 16
file management. 17
Configuration management 18
Configuration management covers various scenarios like Retrieve Resource State, Modify Resource State, Modify Parameters 19
and Retrieve Parameters. NETCONF get-config and edit-config RPCs shall be used for configuration parameter retrieval and 20
updates at the O-RU  21
Performance management 22
Performance management describes the measurements and counters used to  collect data related to O-RU operations. The 23
purpose of Performance Management is optimizing the operation of the O-RU.  24
The measurement results are reported by two options:  25
1. YANG Notification: This option uses the stats definition of YANG model per measurement group. In this case, get 26
rpc and/or notification will be used (see Chapter 7 for more details).  27
2. File Upload: This option uses the file upload procedure defined in File management. The measurement results  are 28
saved to a data file periodically.  29
Fault Management 30
Fault management is responsible for sending alarm notifications to the NETCONF Client. F ault Management allows alarm 31
notifications to be disabled or enabled as well as alarm subscription. 32
File Management 33
File management allows the O-RU Controller to trigger an O-RU to perform upload of files stored on O-RU to O-RU Controller. 34
The O-RU may provide different kinds of files and retrieved files can be used for various purposes. Simultaneous multiple file 35
upload operations can be supported under the same sFTP connection between O-RU to O-DU/SMO. 36
2.2 Interfaces 37
The M-Plane interface is defined between the O-RU Controller and the O-RU. The protocol stack of the M -Plane interface is 38
shown in Figure 3. The transpo rt network layer is built on IP transport and TCP/SSH is used to carry the M -Plane message 39
between the O-RU Controller and the O-RU. As an option, the O -RU may support the capability to support asynchronous 40
notifications to be sent using HTTPS. This option enables system optimization when the O -RU Controller corresponds to the 41
SMO which is operating with a non-persistent NETCONF session to the O-RU. 42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          18
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00

Figure 3 M-plane protocol stack 2
2.3 YANG Module Introduction 3
The data models representing the M -Plane are organized as a set of reusable YANG modules. It is also the intent to reuse the 4
publicly available and generic YANG models as much as possible instead of developing customized O-RAN specific modules. 5
Refer to the various chapters, Annex D and the repository of YANG models for more details on each of these modules.  6
2.4 Security 7
The M-Plane provides end to end security as a mandatory feature. The security is provided using the SSHv2 layer in accordance 8
with RFC 6242  [5]. RFC 6242 provides the procedure for interoperability with NETCONF implementations. If there are 9
multiple NETCONF sessions established with a single O-RU, each session should be established over a separate SSH tunnel. 10

from modifications)

Table 1- M-Plane Security 11
SSHv2 performs server host authentication, key exchange, encryption, and integrity protection. It also derives a unique session 12
ID that may be used by higher -level protocols. The end point authentication should be done as per RFC 4252  [6]. Chapter 3 13
describes the authentication approach based on username and password as well as based on X.509 certificates. 14
The SSHv2 transport level security (encryption algorithms, data integrity algorithms) shall be based on RFC4253  [7]. As per 15
aes128-ctr shall be the mandatory ciphering protocol, and rest of the ones listed as optional. For data integrity, hmac-sha2-256 16
shall be the mandatory algorithm, and rest of the listed algorithms shall be optional. Public key-based host authentication shall 17
be used for authenticating the server (RFC 4253) by the clients, and username/password based client authentication shall be 18
done by the server as part of the SSH session establishment. The O-RU shall support the host key algorithms and key exchange 19
methods defined in section 10.1 of RFC 5656 for securing the Secure Shell (SSH) transport.   20
Note, in order to ensure backwards compatibility with equipment supporting earlier versions of this specification, an 21
operator and vendor may agree to use one of the optional ciphering protocols. 22
As an additional option, both client and server may implement authentication based on X.509 certificates. With this option, 23
RSA 2048 bit shall be supported for the Public Key algorithm, aes 128-ctr shall be supported for the cyphering algorithm and 24
hmac-sha2-256 shall be supported for integrity algorithm. 25
Note, the above specification will be replaced with a cross reference to the O -RAN Security T ask Group Guidelines 26
once such is published. 27

Chapter 3 “Start up” installation  1
This chapter provides the overall start-up mechanism from the power-on of O-RU to available in service. 2
Pre-condition:  3
- Power-ON for O-RU/NETCONF Server or O-RU restart operation.  4
 Power-ON for O-RU controller/NETCONF Client(s) and/or pnfRegistration event-collector. 5
- Physical interface(s) is(are) connected. 6
Post-condition:   7
- O-RU is ready for the radio transmission to the air on at least one carrier if packet transmission received from O-DU  8
- O-RU is ready for the packet transmission to the O-DU if radio reception received at the air on at least one carrier. 9
- At least one O-RU Controller/NETCONF client with either “super-user” or “hybrid-odu” access privileges can control the 10
carrier configuration of the O-RU/NETCONF server in O-RU. 11
 12

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          20
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 1
Figure 4: Overall of Start-Up Installation 2

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          21
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 1
At the power-on of O-RU or following an O-RU restart, the following procedures are performed. 2
1. O-RU performs transport layer resolution (DHCP, MAC, VLAN, IP, etc.) and recovers IP address(es) of O-RU controller(s) 3
and/or pnfRegistration event-collector. 4
2. O-RU begins synchronization of the O-RU against a Primary Reference Clock. (Note: step 2 may be in parallel with step 1 5
for some O-RU implementation.) 6
3. O-RU performs NETCONF Call Home to discovered O-RU controller(s) and/or performs pnfRegistration to discovered 7
event-collector. 8
4. O-RU controller performs SSH connection establishment. 9
5. O-RU and O-RU controller perform NETCONF capability discovery. 10
6. O-RU controller performs optional provisioning of new management accounts (typically only performed once during pre -11
staging) 12
7. O-RU and O-RU controller perform supervision of NETCONF connection. 13
8. O-RU controller performs retrieval of O-RU information. 14
9. O-RU controller performs SW management. 15
10. O-RU controller configures transport connectivity checking on the O-RU, enabling the O-DU to perform C/U-Plane 16
transport connectivity checking between O-DU and O-RU. 17
11. O-RU controller retrieves the O-RU delay profile from the O-RU. 18
12. O-RU controller performs U-Plane configuration between O-DU and O-RU. C/U-Plane transport connectivity between O-19
DU and O-RU is configured as part of this step. 20
13. O-DU optionally performs C/U-Plane delay measurements between O-DU and O-RU if the O-RU supports it. 21
14. O-RU controller performs Fault Management activation. 22
15. O-RU controller activates performance measurement (if required at start-up timing). 23
16. O-RU controller retrieves O-RU state, including synchronization information, from O-RU. 24
17. O-RU controller configures the O-RU operational parameters. 25
18. Service available. 26
Note, the synchronization procedures started in step 2 needs to be completed before service is available. 27
 28
This chapter mainly covers 1 and 3 to 7 as sub-sections. 29
Cross Reference of other chapters: 30
The detail of 2. Synchronization management is described in Chapter 10. 31
The method of 8 and 16 retrieval of O-RU information is described in Chapter 6. 32
The detail of 9. SW management is described in Chapter 5. 33
The detail of 10. C/U-Plane transport connectivity checking between O-DU and O-RU is described in Chapter 4. 34
The detail of 11. Retrieval of the O-RU delay profile and 13. C/U-Plane delay measurements are described in Chapter 4. 35
The detail of 12. U-plane configuration is described in Chapter 12, and C/U-Plane transportation configuration is described in 36
Chapter 4.  37

3.1 Management Plane Transport aspects 4
This sub-section provides the M-plane transport establishment scenario between O-RU and O-RU controller(s), such as O-DU 5
and/or SMO. The transport layer address of M -plane is only the target in this section. Transport aspects of the C plane and U 6
plane are covered in Chapter 4. 7
Pre-condition:  8
- Physical interface is connected. 9
- When operating in an environment using call -home, the NETCONF server and NETCONF Client(s) have an identical 10
NETCONF call home port configured, to ensure the NETCONF client listens on the same port used by the NETCONF Server. 11
Post-condition:   12
- Transport Layer address(es) for M-plane are known to O-RU and O-RU controllers.  13
- O-RU is aware of the physical port(s) for M-plane, e.g., if there are multiple ports in the O-RU. 14
- O-RU is aware of the VLAN(s) to be used for M-Plane, e.g., if VLANs are used in the transport network. 15
- Then O-RU is ready to establish TCP connection for NETCONF call home and/or for PNF registration. 16
For the transport establishment, there are the following alternatives: 17
a) Manual transport layer address configuration in O-RU. This configuration contains the addresses for O-RU and NETCONF 18
client(s) and/or the event-collector. The method to manually configure the O-RU is out of scope in this specification. Assuming 19
manual configuration is successful , the NETCONF server shall be able to  recover this configured information and use the o-20
ran-mplane-int.yang model to communicate this operational-state to a NETCONF client. 21
b) DHCP server provides O-RU’s transport layer address information together with the identity of the NETCONF client and/or 22
the identity of the event-collector. This identity encodes either the transport layer address or FQDN of the NETCONF client or 23
event-collector. If an FQDN is signaled, the O-RU shall use the DNS server address provided by the DHCP server to recover 24
the IP address corresponding to FQDN of the NETCONF client or event-collector. 25
c) If IPv6 is supported, Stateless Address Auto -Configuration (SLAAC) is used to configure the O-RU’s transport address 26
with the DHCP server providing the identity of the NETCONF cl ient and/or event-collector. This identity encodes either the 27
transport layer address or FQDN of the NETCONF client  or event-collector. If an FQDN is signaled, the O-RU shall use the 28
DNS server address provided by the DHCP server to recover the IP address corresponding to FQDN of the NETCONF client  29
or event-collector.  30
Note, a NETCONF client can determine whether an O-RU supports IPv6 by using the get rpc to recover the list of interfaces 31
supported by the O-RU and using the presence of the augmented ipv6 container in the o-ran-interfaces module to indicate IPv6 32
is supported. 33
The O-RU uses the o-ran-dhcp.yang model to be able to expose information signaled by the DHCP server. 34

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          23
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 1
Figure 5: Transport Layer Establishment for M-plane 2

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          24
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
Transport Layer interface related information for M -plane contains at least the physical port number, the hardware address of 1
the Ethernet port, VLAN-ID, local IP address, remote IP address, Default Gateway address and Subnet mask.  2
In the case of option b) and c), the following subsections are used: 3
- O-RU identification in DHCP messages from O-RU. 4
- VLAN discovery aspect for M-plane. 5
- IP address assignment to O-RU. 6
- Discovery of address information of O-RU controller(s) and/or Event-Collector. 7
3.1.1 O-RU identification in DHCP 8
The O-RU shall identify itself to DHCP servers by using DHCP option(s) using the vendor-class-data string within the o-ran-9
dhcp YANG model. For DHCPv4, there are two alternatives. One uses option 60 Vendor Class Identifier , RFC2132 [8]. The 10
other uses option 124 Vendor Identifying Vendor Class Option , RFC3925 [9]. The O-RU shall support at least one of  these 11
options. If the O-RU supports IPv6, then it shall identify itself using the DHCPv6 Vendor Class Option. 12
DHCPv4 Vendor Class Option: 13
• Option: 60 14
• Vendor Class Identifier Option 60: string  15
The format of the vendor class string shall be configured to one of the following three options:  16
1. ““o-ran-ru2/<vendor>, e.g., “o-ran-ru2/vendorA 17
2. “o-ran-ru2/<vendor>/<product-code>”, e.g., “o-ran-ru2/vendorA/ORUAA100 18
3. “o-ran-ru2/<vendor>/<product-code>/<serial-number>”,e.g. , “o-ran-ru2/vendorA/ORUAA100/FR1918010111 19
DHCPv4 Vendor-Identifying Vendor Class Option: 20
• Option: 124 21
• Enterprise number: O-RAN-alliance 53148 22
• Vendor-Class-Data: the format of the string shall follow the rules defined for the DHCPv4 Vendor Class Option 23
DHCPv6 Vendor Class Option: 24
• Option: 16 25
• Enterprise number: O-RAN-alliance 53148 26
• Vendor-Class-Data: the format of the string shall follow the rules defined for the DHCPv4 Vendor Class Option 27
The DHCP Server may use this information when allocating IP a ddresses or when configuring management plane O-RU 28
Controller(s) information in the O-RU. 29
3.1.2 Management Plane VLAN Discovery Aspects 30
The O-RU will be connected to one or more Ethernet ports. The transport systems may be realized such that these Ethernet  31
ports may be configured either as an access port, where untagged Ethernet frames are used, or as a trunk port, where multiple 32
VLANs are configured. At start up, the O-RU will typically not be able to immediately determine whether its ports are attached 33
to remote transport equipment configured for access or trunk mode operation.   34
Once an O-RU completes its boot-up sequence and Ethernet connectivity is detected on at least one of its Ethernet interfaces, 35
the O-RU starts management plane connection establishment. 36

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          25
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
The O-RU needs to determine whether it is connected to an access port or a trunk port. In particular, when connected to a trunk 1
port, the O-RU needs to additionally determine the VLAN identity/ies used to support the management plane communication(s). 2
The VLAN(s) used to support management plane communications can be identified by the DHCP server replying to the DHCP 3
DISCOVER message, as described in sections 3.1.4 and 3.1.6. 4
Note, an O-RU which supports IPv6 may infer that a VLAN is not used to support management plane communications if it 5
receives an IPv6 Router Advertisement without either the “managed address configuration” or “other configuration” bits set. 6
An O-RU may have been previously configured with management plane VLAN information, fo r example storing the last 7
VLAN(s) used for management plane connectivity, and/or being previously configured with a range of management plane 8
VLANs by a NETCONF client that has been stored in reset-persistent memory. The O-RU may use this information to optimize 9
its discovery of the VLAN ID(s) used for management plane connectivity. 10
If the O-RU does not have previously configured management plane VLAN information, the O-RU shall attempt to discover 11
DHCP servers on all of its Ethernet ports using untagged Ethernet frames.  12
If the O-RU does not receive a DHCP OFFER from a DHCP server using untagged frames, or previously configured VLANs, 13
the O-RU should attempt to contact a DHCP server using individual VLANs on all of its Ethernet ports. 14
3.1.3 O-RU Management Plane IP Address Assignment 15
Automatic IP address assignment for the O-RU management plane can be achieved using different techniques: 16
1. IPv4 configuration using DHCPv4, RFC2131 [10] enables DHCP servers to configure IPv4 network address(es) on the O-17
RU. An O-RU shall support the behavior specified in RFC 4361 [33], using stable DHCPv4 node identifiers in their dhcp -18
client-identifier option. 19
Note: a network realized with multiple DHCP servers should ensure that their configurations are coordinated to ensure a 20
common default gateway is provisioned in an O -RU which receives multiple DHCPv4 responses, e.g., when received over 21
different interfaces. 22
Note: an O-RU may indicate that it supports configuration of routing information using RFC 3442, enabling static routes to be 23
used by the O-RU when determining how to route uplink packets, e.g., when the O-RU supports multiple interfaces. 24
For O-RUs that support IPv6, both stateful and stateless address assignment procedures are supported: 25
2. IPv6 Stateless Address Auto-Configuration (SLAAC), RFC4862 [11] enables the O-RU to generate link-local and global 26
addresses. 27
Note: a network realized with multiple IPv6-enabled routers that support dynamic address assignment is expected to use RFC 28
4191 to configure the preference of the default route prefixes learnt by the O-RU using SLAAC. 29
3. IPv6 State-full address configuration uses DHCPv6 , RFC3315 [12] and enables DHCP servers to configure IPv6 network 30
address(es) on the O-RU. DHCPv6 is transported using UDP, using the  link-local address on the O-RU and a link -scoped 31
multicast address on the DHCP server.  32
Note: the above does not restrict the realization of the DHCP server, which may be integrated with the O-DU, may be provided 33
by the transport system, or may be accessed via a relay. 34
The DHCP server should operate using static bindings, i.e., ensuring an O-RU identified by a particular client hardware address 35
will be re-allocated the same management plane IP address, e.g., after performing an O-RU reset procedure. 36
3.1.4 O-RU Controller Discovery 37
This section provides how to automatically discover the O-RU Controller address(es). 38
O-RUs that have obtained their IPv6 addresses by stateless address auto -configuration, shall use stateless DHCPv6, RFC3736 39
[13], to obtain management plane configuration information.  40
Other O-RUs operating using stateful IPv4 or IPv6 address allocations shall obtain management plane configuration information 41
during IP address allocation. 42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          26
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
The O-RU as NETCONF Server shall be able to recover NETCONF Client information using the following DHCP Options , 1
RFC8572 [14]:  2
• DHCPv4 OPTION V4_SZTP_REDIRECT [143] 3
• DHCPv6 OPTION_V6_SZTP_REDIRECT [136] 4
These options are defined in [ 14] and are used to deliver bootstrap -server-list information to the O-RU. The O-RU shall use 5
these options to recover the NETCONF client information using the above IANA defined DHCP options. The O-RU is not 6
required to implement the remainder of the zerotouch capabilities defined in [14].  7
The above DHCP option provi ded information is encoded as a list of one or more server URIs, of the format “https://<ip -8
address-or-hostname>[:<port>]” signaled to the O-RU. The DHCP server shall ensure that all NETCONF client information is 9
encoded with these options. 10
Other O-RUs which have had their IP address(es) manually configured, shall also have their O-RU Controller(s) manually 11
configured. 12
For IPv4, the O-RU may request the OPTION_V4_SZTP_REDIRECT by including its option code in the Parameter Request 13
List (55) in DHCP discover/request messages. 14
For IPv6, the O-RU may request the OPTION_V6_SZTP_REDIRECT option by including the requested option codes in the 15
Option Request Option. 16
Note, these operations are optional because the DHCP server will already be aware that it is communicating with an O-RU 17
based on the recovered vendor class option. 18
To enable O-RUs to operate in legacy environments where the DHCP server has not been enhanced with IANA defined DHCP 19
options for zero touch NETCONF capability, an O-RAN defined vendor specific option can be used to signal all NETCONF 20
client information to the O-RU using option 43 for DHCPv4 and option 17 for DHCPv6.  Multiple instances of NETCONF 21
client information may be signaled, encoded as a sequence of type/length/value fields. 22
The definition of the types used within the DHCPv4 option 43/DHCPv6 Option 17 depends on the vendor-class option reported 23
by the O-RU in its DHCP messages. 24
When a legacy O-RU reports its vendor-class using the “o-ran-ru” prefix, the following types are defined: 25
Type: 0x01 – O-RU Controller IP Address 26
Type: 0x02 – O-RU Controller Fully Qualified Domain Name 27
When the O-RU reports its vendor-class using the “o-ran-ru2” prefix, the following types are defined: 28
Type: 0x81 – O-RU Controller IP Address 29
Type 0x82 – O-RU Controller Fully Qualified Domain Name 30
In all cases, the Type is followed by the length, which is the hexadecimal encoding of length of value field in octets , and the 31
Value. 32
When Type corresponds to an O -RU Controller IP Address , the value encodes IPv4 address(es) in hexadecimal format. For 33
example, a single server with IPv4 address 198.185.159.144 will be encoded in an option 43 TLV as 34
Type 0x81 (or x01 for legacy) 35
Length: 0x04  36
Value: C6 B9 9F 90 37
When Type corresponds to an O-RU Controller Fully Qualified Domain Name, this encodes the string representation of domain 38
name, using ACSII encoding (i.e., following for encoding used for the domain name in the Host Name DHCP Option 12). For 39
example, a server with FQDN “controller.operator.com” will be encoded in an option 43 TLV as 40
Type 0x82 (or x02 for legacy)  41
Length: 0x17  42

Value: 63 6F 6E 74 72 6F 6C 6C 65 72 2E 6F 70 65 72 61 74 6F 72 2E 63 6F 6D 1
The format of the DHCPv6 option 17 follows the format of the DHCPv4 encoding, with the additional inclusion of an Enterprise 2
Number prior to the TLV option data. The IANA allocated private enterprise number to be used with DHCPv6 option 17 is 3
53148. 4
3.1.5 Multi-Vendor Plug-and-Play 5
As described in sub-section 3.3.2, an O-RU may optionally support certificate enrollment using CMPv2. 3GPP 32.509 6
specifies how the O-RU can discover the IP address or FQDN of one or more Certification Authority (CA/RA) servers using 7
DHCP Option 43. 8
In addition to the DHCPv4 encoding using Option 43, an O-RU supporting IPv6 and certificate enrollment using CMPv2 9
shall additionally support the signaling of vendor specific options using DHCPv6 option 17. The format of the DHCPv6 10
option 17 follows the format of the DHCPv4 encoding, with the additional inclusion of an Enterprise Number prior to the 11
TLV option data. The IANA allocated private enterprise number to be used with DHCPv6 option 17 is 53148 (as allocated by 12
IANA to O-RAN Alliance). 13
An O-RU shall report any discovered multi-vendor plug-and-play servers using the o-ran-dhcp YANG model. 14
3.1.6 Event-Collector Discovery  15
This section describes how an O -RU automatically discovers the Event-Collector to which it shall send i ts pnfRegistration 16
event. The support by an O -RU of PNF Registration to a discovered Event-Collector is optional and hence this section only 17
applies to those O-RUs that support this optional capability.  18
O-RUs that have obtained their IPv6 addresses by sta teless address auto-configuration, shall use stateless DHCPv6, RFC3736 19
[13], to obtain Event-Collector information. Other O-RUs operating using stateful IPv4 or IPv6 address allocations shall obtain 20
Event-Collector information during IP address allocation.  Other O -RUs which have had their IP address(es) manually 21
configured, shall also have their Event-Collector(s) and Event-Collector Notification Format manually configured. 22
The O-RU shall be able to recover Event-Collector information using O-RAN defined vendor specific option to signal Event-23
Collector information to the O-RU using option 43 for DHCPv4 and option 17 for DHCPv6.  24
The definition of the types used within the DHCPv4 option 43/DHCPv6 Option 17 are as follows: 25
Type: 0x83 – Event-Collector IP Address 26
Type: 0x84 – Event-Collector Fully Qualified Domain Name 27
Type: 0x85 – Event-Collector Notification Format 28
In this version of the specification, the operation of an O -RU when receiving multiple instances of the Event-Collector IP 29
Address and/or Event-Collector FQDN information is not defined. 30
In all cases, the Type is followed by the length, which is the hexade cimal encoding of length of value field in octets, and the 31
Value. 32
When Type corresponds to an Event-Collector IP Address, the value encodes IPv4 address(es) in hexadecimal format. For 33
example, an Event-Collector with IPv4 address 198.185.159.144 will be encoded in an option 43 TLV as 34
Type 0x83 35
Length: 0x04  36
Value: C6 B9 9F 90 37
When Type corresponds to an Event-Collector Fully Qualified Domain Name, this encodes the string representation of domain 38
name, using ACSII encoding (i.e., following for encoding used for the domain name in the Host Name DHCP Option 12). For 39
example, a server with FQDN “collector.operator.com” will be encoded in an option 43 TLV as 40
Type 0x84 41

In this version of the specification, the operation of an O -RU when receiving an Event-Collector FQDN that is subsequently 3

The format of the DHCPv6 option 17 follows the format of the DHCPv4 encoding, with the additional inclusion of an Enterprise 5

3.2 NETCONF Call Home to O-RU Controller(s) 17
The O-RU aims to have NETCONF sessions with all of the known O-RU Controller(s), either discovered using the DHCP 18
options defined in Section 3.1.4 , provisioned by an existing NETCONF client , or statically configured.  An O-RU controller 19
may attempt to autonomously initiate a NETCONF session with the O-RU, e.g., triggered by the pnfRegistration procedure. In 20
order to support NETCONF clients corresponding to known O-RU Controllers that either do not attempt to initiate a NETCONF 21
session with the O-RU, or are prohibited from doing so, e.g., because of Network Address Translation limitations, the O-RU 22
shall call home to all known O-RU Controllers with which it does not already have an active NETCONF session. 23
If the O-RU is unable to establish a NETCONF session with any of the O-RU Controller(s), the O-RU shall use the “re-call-24
home-no-ssh-timer” to repeatedly re -perform the call home procedure to all with wh ich is does not have an established 25
NETCONF session.  26
The O-RU shall use RFC 8071 [15] whereby the O-RU (NETCONF Server) initiates a TCP connection to the NETCONF client. 27
The port used by the O-RU shall be the one signaled using the RFC 8572 DHCP option [14], else, if no port was signaled, the 28
O-RU shall use the IANA-assigned port 4334. When the NETCONF client accepts a TCP connection on the allocated port, it 29
initiates an SSH session with the NETC ONF Server. Using this SSH session, the NETCONF client initiates a NETCONF 30
session. 31

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          29
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
The O-RU shall ensure that a persistent connection to any NETCONF client with “sudo” privileges is maintained by actively 1
testing the aliveness of the connection using the keep-alive mechanism defined in [15]. The establishment of NETCONF client 2
privileges is covered in Section 3.4. 3
3.3 SSH Connection Establishment 4
The identity of the SSH server (O-RU) shall be verified and authenticated by the SSH client (NETCONF client) according to 5
local policy before password -based authentication data or any configuration or state data is sent to or received from the SSH 6
server.  7
Public key-based host authentication shall be used for authenticating the server (RFC 4253) by the clients. In addition, server 8
authentication based on X.509 certificates may also be provided [31]. 9
Note: Public key-based host authentication requires that the SSH server (O-RU) public keys are provisioned in the NETCONF 10
client (e.g., O-DU and/or SMO). As an alternative , RFC4251 mentions that “a possible strategy is to only accept a host key 11
without checking the first time a host is connected, save the key in a local database, and compare against that key on all future 12
connections to that host.”. This option simplifies the key management procedure as it doesn’t require to pre -populate them in 13
O-DU/SMO (SSH client) but obviously at the price of degraded security, therefore the support  of this option shall be 14
configurable and left to operator’s choice. 15
3.3.1 NETCONF Security 16
In this version of O-RU Management Plane Specification, the security of the NETCONF protocol is realized using SSHv2. O-17
RAN NETCONF implementations shall implement RFC 6242 [5] that addresses earlier delimiter issues when using RFC 4742. 18
As the default, the  NETCONF Server in the  O-RU shall provide access to the NETCONF subsystem only when using SSH 19
established using the IANA -assigned TCP port 830 [ 5]. The O-RU may be configured to additionally allow access to the 20
NETCONF subsystem over other ports. 21
If multiple NETCONF sessions are established to an O-RU, those sessions shall be established over separate SSH tunnels. 22
3.3.2 NETCONF Authentication 23
This version of the O-RU Management Plane Specification uses password authentication method for SSHv2 [ 6]. In addition, 24
client authentication based on X.509 certificates should also be provided [31]. 25
If authentication is based on X.509 certificates, for the purposes of user authe ntication, the mapping between certificates and 26
user names is provided by the SubjectAltName field of the X.509 certificate, which means that the user name is coded in the 27
subjectAltName. The username is determined from the subjectAltName using the rules defined in RFC 7589. 28
Upon initial system initialization, the O-RU is configured with a default account. The specific details of the default account are 29
to be agreed between operator and vendor. An example of a default user account for account-type PASSWORD is one with 30
username “oranuser”. An example of a default user account for account -type CERTIFICATE is map type “san-rfc822-name” 31
with an rfc822-name of “oranuser@o-ran.org”. 32
The default account may be of account -type PASSWORD, in which case a default passw ord also needs to be defined and 33
configured in the O-RU, for example “o-ran-password”. 34
Note: As the default account may be operator specific, this may require that the O-RU provides facilities to configure securely 35
this default account at installation time (i.e. before the O-RU is connected to the O-RU Controller). 36
The default account is a member of the “sudo” access control group (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges) as it can 37
be used to create other accounts (see Section 3.3.3). 38
The identity of the SSH client (NETCONF client) shall be verified and authenticated by the SSH server ( O-RU) according to 39
local policy to ensure that the incoming SSH client request is legitimate before any configuration or state data is sent to o r 40
received from the SSH client.  41
Upon initial system initialization, the NETCONF client can authenticate itself to the O-RU using SSH Authentication, with the 42
agreed default username and password. 43

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          31
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
If authentication based on X.509 certificates according to [31] is supported by SSH client and server, the certificates need to be 1
installed at initial system initialization, or can be obtained through certificate enrolment with operator’s PKI (certificate  2
enrolment as defined by 3GPP with CMPv2 protocol between the NE and the operator’s CA). 3
3.3.3 User Account Provisioning 4
The NETCONF client with suitable privileges may provision user accounts on the O-RU, including the accounts (users) name, 5
password, group (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges) and whether a particular account is enabled or disabled.  6
• The username name is a string between 3 -32 characters. The first character must be a lowercase letter. The remaining 7
characters can be a lowercase letter or a number.  8
• The account-type is an enumeration, indicating whether password or certificate -based authentication is used for this 9
account. 10
• The password is a string between 8 -128 characters. Allowed characters in the password field include lowercase and 11
uppercase letters, numbers and the special characters: ! $ % ^ ( ) _ + ~ { } [ ] . – The password leaf is not present for those 12
user accounts associated with certificate-based authentication. 13
• The access control group associated with an account (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges). 14
• Whether an account is enabled. The YANG model ensures that at least one user account is always enabled on the O-RU 15
The new account information (user name, password, access group and whether the account is enabled) shall be stored in reset-16
persistent memory in O-RU. 17
When certificate based client authentication is used no password needs to be provisioned. At time of SSH connection, user’s 18
authorization is done based on the X.509 certificate’s SubjectAltName field that codes the associated account’s name. 19
When other user account (sudo) is created, the NETCONF client closes existing NETCONF session as described in section 3.7. 20
Then, the O-RU disables the default account and default account stays disabled over the resets. The default account becomes 21
enabled when the O-RU is reset to the factory default software by following the procedures defined in subsection 5.7. Any other 22
way to enable the default account is not precluded as O-RU vendor implementation matter. 23
3.4 NETCONF Access Control 24
This subsection defines the access control for NETCONF clients. Its motivation is that when multiple NETCONF clients (users) 25
are defined, the NETCONF access control mechanism enables the NETCONF server to limit some operations for one client but 26
allow full access for another client. In particular, for hybrid access configuration as introduced in Chapter 2, this allows the 27
privileges associated with the NETCONF client in the O-DU to be distinct and different from the privileges associated with the 28
NETCONF client in the SMO. 29
In order to support interoperable access control management, the NETCONF Server shall use the IETF NETCONF Access 30
Control Model [RFC8341]. 31
Currently six access control groups are defined per SSH session: “sudo”, “smo”, “hybrid-odu”, “nms”, “fm-pm”, and “swm”. 32
The table below maps the group name to different privileges. Privileges are defined per namespace for read “R”, write “W” 33
and execute “X” rpc operations or subscribe to Notifications.  34
Note: when operating in hybrid management, the definition of above groupings does not preclude the NETCONF client in a 35
centralized network management system from being configured “sudo” privilege s that permit it to edit the configuration used 36
by an O-RU. However, importantly the operation of the O -DU in those situations may not be defined. For example, an O -DU 37
when operating with an O-RU which receives an autonomous reset RPC from a centralized NM S may not result in the O -DU 38
recovering the o-ran-operations:operational-info/operational-state/restart-cause from the O-RU to then determine that an 39
NMS triggered reset has been performed.  In order to reduce the possibility of such a scenario, it is recom mended that when 40
operating in hybrid mode of operation, the NETCONF client in the O -DU is associated with the “hybrid-odu” privilege group 41
and the NETCONF client in the SMO is associated with the “smo” privilege group. 42

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.

3.5 NETCONF capability discovery 5
The O-RU advertises its NETCONF capabilities in the NETCONF Hello message. The Hello message provides an indication 6
of support for standard features defined in NETCONF RFCs as well as support for specific namespaces. 7
NETCONF capabilities are exchanged between the O-RU and the NETCONF client(s). Examples of capabilities include [3]: 8
• Writable-running Capability 9
• Candidate Configuration Capability and associated Commit operation 10
• Discard change operation 11
• Lock and un-lock operations 12
• Confirmed commit Capability 13
• Cancel commit operation 14
• Rollback on error capability 15
• Validate Capability 16
• Startup configuration capability 17
• URL capability 18
• XPATH capability 19
• Notifications 20
• Interleave capability 21
All O-RAN O-RUs shall support the XPATH capability, NETCONF Notifications and at least one of the writeable-running and 22
candidate configuration capabilities. 23
The NETCONF client uses the get RPC together with sub-tree based <filter> and XPATH based <filter> to recover particular 24
sub-trees from the O-RU. Please see Chapter 6 for more information on NETCONF based configuration management. 25
In order to avoid interactions between the operation of supervision watchdog timer (see section 3.6) and the confirmed commit 26
timer (default value set to 600 seconds in RFC 6241), when using the NETCONF confirmed commit capability, a NECTONF 27
client with “sudo” privileges shall ensure the confirmed -timeout is les s than the supervision-notification-interval timer 28
(default value 60 seconds in o-ran-supervision.yang).  29

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          34
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
3.6 Monitoring NETCONF connectivity 1
When having a session with a NETCONF client with “sudo” or “hybrid-odu” access privileges, the O-RU operates a watchdog 2
supervision timer to ensure that the session to the NECTONF client is persistent, as described in section 3.4. Additionally, the 3
O-RU provides NETCONF Notifications to indicate to remote systems that its management system is operational. This 4
supervision is intended to be used with the NETCONF client associated with the operation of the peer to the O-RAN Radio’s 5
lower layer split. 6
Note, if another NETCONF client is discovered or configured, e.g., in hybrid mode of operation, and is used to establish 7
a NETCONF session with “sudo” access privileges, the same watchdog supervision rules shall apply, meaning that a 8
NETCONF server shall support the operation of individual supervision watchdog timers for each NETCONF client with 9
“sudo” or “hybrid-odu” privileges . 10
The NETCONF client is responsible for automatically enabling the operation of the supervision watchdog timer  by creating 11
supervision-notification subscription, whenever the O-RU has an established NETCONF session to a client with “sudo” or 12
“hybrid-odu” privileges.  13
The O-RU uses two timers, referred generically as watchdog timers, to support the bi -directional monitoring of NETCONF  14
connectivity; 15
• Notification timer: 16
Value: Equal to supervision-notification-interval (default value: 60s) 17
Operation: The O-RU sends supervision-notification to those NETCONF clients that have subscribed to receive such 18
notifications. The O-RU sends supervision-notification, at the latest when the timer expires. The O -RU Controller 19
confirms that NETCONF connectivity to the O-RU is operational by receiving the notification.  20
• Supervision timer: 21
Value : Equal to supervision-notification-interval (default value: 60s) + guard-timer-overhead (default : 10s) 22
Operation: The O-RU goes into supervision failure operation when the timer expires. This means that a NETCONF 23
client with sudo privileges should repeatedly reset this supervision timer. The O-RU confirms that NETCONF 24
connectivity to the O-RU Controller is operational.  25
 26
The O-RU enables watchdog timers when it receives an rpc create-subscription from a NETCONF client with sudo privileges. 27
The notification timer shall start when the O -RU receives a create -subscription rpc, but how the O -RU treats the supervision 28
timer is up to O-RU’s implementation based on the above definition. After the watchdog timers have been enabled, the O-RU 29
is responsible for sending supervision-notification after the expiry of the notification timer. An O-RU Controller with “sudo” 30
or “hybrid-odu” privileges shall be prepared to receive supervision-notification at any time when the watchdog timers are 31
enabled. 32
The NETCONF client is responsible for sending supervision-watchdog-reset RPC in order not to cause the Supervision timer 33
to expire, and the O-RU should send next notification timestamp  as next-update-at in reply. (Note : next-update-at is just 34
informative). In the supervision-watchdog-reset RPC, the NETCONF client may configure new value s for the watchdog 35
timers. When the O-RU receives an rpc supervision-watchdog-reset, it is responsible for resetting its supervision timer and 36
notification timer. 37
The NETCONF client can set new value of watchdog timer without receiving supervision-notification from the O-RU. The 38
new value is taken into use immediately with respect to supervision-watchdog-reset RPC content. The next notification should 39
be expected not later than at the moment addressed in timestamp provided by RPC reply. 40
Note, if another NETCONF client has locked th e running configuration, e.g., when operating in hybrid mode of 41
operation, and if the O -RU Controller attempts to configure a new value of the watchdog timer(s) by sending the 42
supervision-watchdog-reset RPC, then the RPC operation to reset the watchdog tim er will succeed, but the related 43
backend implementation to modify the watchdog timer(s) may fail. In such circumstances, the O-RU may use the error-44
message in the RPC output to indicate to the O-RU Controller that the configuration modification has failed. 45
If the supervision timer expires, the O-RU will enter “supervision failure” condition, as described in Chapter 11 . If all 46
NETCONF sessions to NECTONF clients with “sudo” privileges are closed, the O-RU shall immediately disable operation of 47
the supervision timer. 48

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          35
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00

3.7 Closing a NETCONF Session 4
A NETCONF client closes an existing NETCONF session by issuing the RPC close-session command. The O-RU shall respond 5
and close the SSH session. The O-RU shall then re-commence call home procedures, as described in Section 3.2. 6
Note, under normal operations, it is expect ed that at least one NETCONF session with “sudo” or “hybrid-odu” privileges is 7
long-lived and used to repeatedly reset the O-RU’s supervision watchdog timer.  NECTONF clients associated with other  8
privilege groups are not expected to operate using persistent NETCONF sessions. 9
Note, if a NETCONF client has been previously become known to an O -RU by being configured using NETCONF, and the 10
NETCONF client is subsequently removed from the O -RU’s configuration, e.g., by a second NETCONF client with “sudo” 11
privileges, the NETCONF server shall force the termination of the NETCONF session to the removed client.  12
3.8 PNF Registration  13
The support by an O-RU of PNF Registration to a discovered Event-Collector is optional and hence this section only applies to 14
those O-RUs that support this optional capability. An O-RU that support pnfRegistration shall also support the Monitoring the 15
Communications Channel between O-RU and Event-Collector as defined in sub-section 15.6. 16
3.8.1 PNF Registration Procedure 17
The pnfRegistration notification is a JSON encoded message sent from the O -RU to the discovered Event-Collector using 18
REST/HTTPS. When performing PNF Registration, the O -RU shall send the pnfRegistration notificati on to all discovered  19
Event-Collectors. The sending of the pnfRegistration event is repeated periodically until the O-RU receives a request to establish 20
a NETCONF session from the SMO. 21
