Chapter 4 O-RU to O-DU Interface Management  12
An O -RU has a number of network interfaces, including Ethernet , VLAN  and IP interfaces . This section describes the 13
management of these network interfaces.  14
4.1 O-RU Interfaces 15
The O-RU’s configuration for its interfaces is defined using the o-ran-interfaces.yang module. This module augments the 16
standard ietf -interfaces.yang and ietf -ip.yang modules. The O-RU’s interfaces are built on a layering principle  where each 17
interface has a unique name.  18
All interfaces are referenced by their port-number and name. The base interface corresponds to the Ethernet interface. These 19
leafs describe the maximum transmission unit (l2-mtu), the hardware-address as well as optional alias mac addressees that may 20
be used to transport the CU plane. Above the Ethernet interface are VLAN interfaces. Both Ethernet and VLAN interfaces can 21
support IP interfaces. IP interfaces are defined using the standard ietf -ip.yang model. Accordingly, each IP interface can have 22
an IPv4 and/or optional IPv6 interface(s) defined. Operational state associated with these interfaces provide additional detail of 23
the layer 3 configuration, including prefix(es), domain name servers and default gateway addresses. 24
Finally, leafs associated with CoS and DSCP marking are defined, enabling independent configuration of CoS and DS CP 25
markings for u-plane, c -plane and m -plane traffic. As a default, all user -plane flows are marked identically by the O-RU. 26

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          38
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
Optionally, the interfaces can be configured to support enhanced user plane marking for up -link traffic whereby different CoS 1
or DSCP values can be configured. This enables individual receive endpoints in the O-RU to be configured with different 2
markings to then enable differentiated handling of up-link flows by the transport system. 3
Because the o-ran-interfaces model defines augments to the ietf -interfaces model, the O-RU can leverage the definition of 4
operational state in ietf-interfaces to optionally report packet and byte counts on a per interface basis. A single RPC is defined 5
in the o-ran-interfaces module, to enable these counters to be reset. 6
4.2 Transceiver 7
The o-ran-transceiver YANG module is used to define operational state for the pluggable transceiver module (like SFP, SFP+, 8
SFP28, XFP and QSFP, QSFP+, QSFP28, QSFP56 ). Each transceiver is associated with a unique interface-name and port-9
number. 10
A digital diagnostic monitoring interface for optical transceivers is used to allow acce ss to device operating parameters. As 11
specified in SFF-8472 [16] and SFF-8636 [34], data is typically retrieved from the transceiver module in a file. This file may 12
be obtained from O-RU by the NETCONF client. Please see Chapter 9 for more details. 13
With QSFP form factor, the optical links may be multi -wavelengths (4xTx & 4xRx) and/or multi -fibers (MPO - Multifiber 14
Parallel Optic). The QSFP digital diagnostic interface [34] describes the use of optical lanes and the O -RU interface 15
management defines alarm 29 :“transceiver fault” for all media lanes. 16
The byte with offset i (i=0, …, 511) from the beginning of the file is the byte read from data address i of the transceiver memory 17
at two-wire interface address 0xA0 if i<256, otherwise it is the byte read from data address i-256 of the transceiver memory at 18
two-wire interface address 0xA2. The retrieved data is stored in the file without any conversion in binary format. 19
The O-RU stores data from the transceiver module on transceiver module detection during startup. The data from the transceiver 20
module is saved in the file. A NETCONF client can upload it by using the File Upload procedure defined in chapter 9. The O-21
RU does not synchronize contents of the file with transceiver memory in runtime, therefore byt es representing dynamic 22
information are expected to be outdated . The O-RU does not remove the file on transceiver module removal. If a transceiver 23
module is inserted during File Upload procedure then the procedure may provide a file with previous content or fail (with failure 24
reason as listed in File Upload procedure). If the O-RU is unable to retrieve the data from the transceiver module or it is not 25
present then the O-RU does not create the file or removes the file created earlier (note that File Upload p rocedure requesting 26
non-existing file shall fail).  27
The file name shall have the following syntax: 28
sfp_{portNumber}.sffcap 29
where {portNumber} is the value of port-number leaf of the corresponding list of port -transceiver data. Examples: 30
sfp_0.sffcap, sfp_1.sffcap. 31
4.3 C/U Plane VLAN Configuration 32
Within the o-ran-interfaces YANG model, each named Ethernet interface includes a leaf to indicate whether VLAN tagging is 33
supported. By default, VLAN tagging is enabled on all interfaces. This permits an O-RU to autonomously discover that it is 34
connected to a trunk port, as described in Section 3.1.2. 35
When an O-RU is connected to a trunk port, VLANs will also typically be assigned to the C/U plane connections. The VLAN(s) 36
used to support C/U plane transport may be different from the VLAN(s) used to support management plane connectivity. When 37
different VLANs are used, the C/U plane VLANs shall be configured in the O-RU by the NETCON F client. In such 38
circumstances, as defined in o-ran-interfaces, the NETCONF client shall configure separate named interfaces for each active 39
VLAN. This configuration will define a C/U-Plane named VLAN interface as being the higher-layer-if reference for t he 40
underlying Ethernet interface and the underlying Ethernet interface is defined as being the lower-layer-if reference for the 41
named VLAN interface. 42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          39
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
4.4 O-RU C/U Plane IP Address Assignment 1
In this release, the support for C/U plane transport over UDP/IP is optional and hence this section only applies to those O-RUs 2
that support this optional capability. 3
An O-RU that supports C/U plane transport over UDP/IP shall support IPv4 and optionally IPv6 based transport. A NETCONF 4
client can determine whether an O-RU supports IPv6 by using the get rpc to recover the list of interfaces supported by the O-5
RU and using the presence of the augmented ipv6 container in the o-ran-interfaces YANG module to indicate IPv6 is supported. 6
The IP interface(s) used to support UDP/IP based C/U plane transport may be different than the IP interface(s) used to support 7
management plane connectivity. When different IP interface(s) is/are used, the C/U plane IP interfaces shall be configured in  8
the O-RU by the NETCONF client by using the ietf-ip YANG model to configure the IPv4 container and/or IPv6 container. 9
When defined by the NETCONF client, this interface shall be configured using either a named Ethernet interface (i.e., where 10
the interface type is set to ianaift:ethernetCsmacd) and/or a named VLAN interface  (i.e., where the interface type is set to 11
ianaift:l2vlan), depending upon whether VLANs are used to support IP based C/U plane traffic. 12
When a separate C/U plane IP interface is configured by the NETCONF client, additionally the NETCONF client may statically 13
configure the IP address(es) on this/these interface(s). If the NETCONF client does not statically configure an IP address, the 14
O-RU shall be responsible for performing IP address assignment procedures on the configured interfaces. 15
When an O-RU has not been configured with a static IP address , the O-RU shall support the IP address assignment using the 16
following techniques: 17
1. IPv4 configuration using DHCPv4 [10]. 18
And when the O-RU supports IPv6: 19
2. IPv6 Stateless Address Auto-Configuration (SLAAC) [11]. 20
3. IPv6 State-full address configuration uses DHCPv6 [12]. 21
4.5 Definition of processing elements 22
The CU-plane application needs to be uniquely associated with specific data flows. This association is achieved by defining an 23
O-RU “processing element” which can then be associated with a particular C /U plane endpoint address [2] or delay 24
measurement operation. 25
The O-RU management plane supports different options for defining the transpo rt-based endpoint identifiers used by a 26
particular processing element (used depending on transport environment), supporting the following 3 options: 27
• Processing element definition based on usage of different (alias) MAC addresses; 28
• Processing element definition based on a combination of VLAN identity and MAC address; and 29
• Processing element definition based on UDP-ports and IP addresses. 30
Note: there is no well-defined source port currently allocated by IANA for the o-ran application and hence the NETCONF 31
client is responsible for configuring this port number in the O-RU.  32
A processing element defines both the local and remote endpoints use d with a specific data flow. The processing element 33
definition includes its element name which is then used by other systems to refer to a particular processing element instance. 34
The o-ran-interfaces YANG model is used to define feature support for C/U plane transport based on alias MAC addresses and 35
UDP/IP. The exchange of NETCONF capabilities is used to signal which optional capabilities are supported by the O-RU, as 36
described in Annex C. 37
The o-ran-processing-elements YANG model uses a processing-elements container to define a list of processing elements. 38
Each processing element is identified by a unique element  name. Each processing element references a particular interface-39
name used to support the data flows associated with a particular processing element. Depending upon the type of C/U plane 40
transport session, additionally leafs are configured that specify MAC addresses, and/or VLANs and/or IP addresses and/or UDP 41
ports used to identify a particular processing element. 42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          40
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
4.6 O-DU Verification of C/U Plane Transport Connectivity  1
As described above, there will likely be multiple C/U -plane data flows being exchanged between the O-DU and the O-RU. In 2
order to enable checks verifying end-to-end transport connectivity between the O-DU and O-RU, the O-RU shall support 3
transport connectivity check capabilities using a request/reply function.  4
Using that connectivity monitoring procedure, reachability/connectivity checks between user plane endpoints can be performed 5
by the O-DU: 6
- During O-RU configuration, to validate the transport configuration 7
- At runtime to monitor network connectivity 8
In packet networks connectivity checking is usually done by exchanging probe-messages between the endpoints. The periodicity 9
of this exchange depends on the use case. For availability measurement, the only use case relevant for this specification, the 10
periodicity is usually between 1 and 60 seconds. 11
Two different network protocols are defined for performing the transport connectivity check procedure: 12
- For C/U sessions over Ethernet: Loop -back Protocol (LB/LBM) as defined by IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802.1ag) 13
[17]. 14
- When the O-RU supports C/U sessions over IP: UDP echo, RFC 862 [18]. 15
 16
Figure 9: C/U Plane Transport Connectivity Verification 17
4.6.1 Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure 18
If the O-RU and O-DU are operating their C/U sessions on Ethernet, the transport connectivity verification checks operate at 19
the Ethernet layer. In this O-RU Management Plane Specification, the protocol for Ethernet connectivity monitoring is based 20
on the Loop-back Protocol as defined by IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802.1ag) [17].  21
For the purpose of connectivity monitoring all C/U -plane messaging endpoints in the fronthaul network are part of the same 22
Maintenance Entity (ME). They each get the assigned the role of a Maintenance association End Point (MEP) for LBM. 23

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          41
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
The sending of Loop-back Messages (LBMs) is administratively initiated and stopped in the O-DU. Therefore, sending LBM 1
requests needs to be requested by an administration entity, specifying an Ethernet MAC address assigned to the O-RU responder. 2
In this O-RU Management Plane Specification requests a re always sent from an O-DU to a unicast Ethernet MAC address of 3
an O-RU. 4
4.6.1.1 Validating the transport configuration 5
After setting up a U/C-plane session between an O-DU and an O-RU, the O-DU can test whether connectivity exists as per the 6
configuration. To achieve that, at the time a U/C-plane messaging endpoint becomes operational at an O-RU, it starts an LBM 7
responder application which automatically responds to incoming LBM requests on that end point. Based on a configuration 8
command the O-DU starts sending out a predefined number of LBM requests to its O-RU(s) at a predefined interval, storing 9
the information received in LBM responses from the O-RU(s) in an internal database. O-RU(s) are identified by both Ethernet 10
MAC address and the CU plane VLAN.  11
Note, the O-RU shall be able to respond to LoopBack Messages received from different remote Maintenance Association 12
Endpoints 13
In case the configuration of the session is indeed correct, the O-DU should receive LBM responses from the O-RU(s) within a 14
time frame dependent on the network latency and the O-RU’s reaction time. If LBMs from the O-RU(s) are being received, the 15
session is determined to be operational. 16
4.6.1.2 Monitor network connectivity 17
After the procedure described in section 4.6.1.1 has been executed successfully, a further procedure may be executed 18
continuously to maintain the connectivity status. To achieve this the O-DU continues to send out LBM requests at the configured 19
interval. It also keeps track of LBM responses received.  20
Based on the LBM responses received the O-DU shall decide on the connectivity status. Connectivity shall be assumed to be 21
available as long as LBM responses from the O-RU(s) are being received at the configured in terval. Connectivity shall be 22
assumed not available if no LBM response from the particular O-RU has been received for an interval that is as long as 3 x the 23
configured LBM request interval or longer. 24
4.6.1.3 Managing Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure 25
An O-DU may have one or more Ethernet interfaces that have to support the Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure. This 26
section describes the management of this function. The module described here is based on (i.e. a subset of) the mef-cfm module 27
defined by the Metro Ethernet Forum [19]. This is to allow for a later extension of the module to the full feature set of mef-cfm.  28
The YANG module provided below supports the configuration and fault management of the Loop-back Protocol as defined by 29
IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802.1ag). 30
Derived from MEF CFM YANG, the subset of type definitions are defined as part of the o-ran-lbm.yang. 31
4.6.2 IP connectivity monitoring procedure 32
If the O-RU and O-DU are connected using IP (and UDP/IP is being used to transp ort the C/U plane), these transport 33
connectivity verification checks operate at layer 3. Layer 3 connection verification is based on the O-RU supporting the UDP 34
echo server functionality, RFC 862 [18]. The NETCONF client is responsible for enabling the UDP  echo server in the O-RU, 35
triggering the O-RU to listen for UDP datagrams on the well-known port 7. When a datagram is received by the O-RU, the data 36
from it is sent back towards the sender, where its receipt can be used to confirm UDP/IP connectivity between the endpoints. 37
4.6.2.1 Managing IP Connectivity Monitoring Procedure 38
This section describes the management of the UDP echo functionality. The NETCONF client uses the enable-udp-echo leaf in 39
the udp-echo YANG model to control operation of the UDP echo server in the O-RU. The NETCONF client is able to control 40
the DSCP marking used by the O-RU when it echoes back datagrams using the dscp-config leaf. Additionally, the NETCONF 41
client can recover the number of UDP Echo messages sent by the O-RU by using echo-replies-transmitted operational state. 42
An O-DU may have one or more IP interfaces that have to support the UDP/IP connectivity monitoring procedure. An O-RU 43
with its UDP echo server enabled shall be able to respond to UDP datagrams originated from any valid source IP address. 44

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          42
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
4.7 C/U-Plane Delay Management  1
The Intra-PHY lower layer fronthaul split has the characteristic of a stringent bandwidth and tight latency requirement. The 2
CUS-Plane specification [2] describes how the propagation delay incurred due to distance between the O-DU and O-RU is an 3
important parameter in defining the optimization of windowing and receive -side buffering operations. This section describes 4
the procedures that are used to manage the delay parameters for the fronthaul split.  5
4.7.1 Delay Parameters 6
The reference points for delay management are introduced in [2] and included for reference in Figure 10. 7
 8
Figure 10: Definition of reference points for delay management 9
Important delay parameters related to the operation of the O-RU are referred to as the O-RU delay profile. As the delay 10
characteristics for an O-RU may vary based on air interface properties, a table of the parameters is provided based on a 11
combination of sub -carrier spacing (SCS) and channel bandwidth . When considering the downlink data direction, these 12
parameters include: 13
T2a_min :  Corresponding t o the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving the last data sample over the 14
fronthaul interface and transmitting the first IQ sample at the antenna. 15
T2a_max: Corresponding to the earliest allowable time when a data packet is received before th e corresponding firs IQ 16
sample is transmitted at the antenna. 17
Using the above parameters, (T2a_max – T2a_min): The difference between these two parameters corresponds to the O-RU 18
reception window range. 19
T2a_min_cp_dl: Corresponding to the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving downlink real time control 20
plane message over the fronthaul interface and transmitting the corresponding first IQ sample at the antenna. 21
T2a_max_cp_dl: Corresponding to the earliest allowable time when a downlink real time control message is received before 22
the corresponding first IQ sample is transmitted at the antenna. 23
Tcp_adv_dl: Corresponding to the time difference (advance) between the reception window for downlink real time Control 24
messages and reception window for the corresponding IQ data messages. 25
The delay parameters related to the operation of the O-RU for the uplink data direction include: 26
Ta3_min: Corresponding to the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving an IQ sample at the antenna and 27
transmitting the first data sample over the fronthaul interface. 28
Ta3_max: Corresponding to the maximum O-RU data processing delay between receiving an IQ sample at the antenna and 29
transmitting the last data sample over the fronthaul interface. 30
Using the above parameters, (Ta3_max – Ta3_min): The difference between these two parameters corresponds to the O-RU 31
transmission window range. 32
T2a_min_cp_ul: The minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving real time up-link control plane message over 33
the fronthaul interface and receiving the first IQ sample at the antenna. 34
T2a_max_cp_ul: The earliest allowable time when a real time up-link control message is received before the corresponding 35
first IQ sample is received at the antenna. 36

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          43
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
When requested, all O-RUs shall signal the table of statically “pre -defined” values of the above parameters, for different 1
supported combinations of SCS and channel bandwidth over the management plane interface. This will typically occur during 2
the initial startup phase. 3
4.7.2 Reception Window Monitoring 4
The O-RU shall monitor operation of its reception window, monitoring the arrival of packets received over the fronthaul 5
interface relative to the earliest and latest allowable times as defined by the values of T2a_max and T2a_min respectively. 6
See Annex B.2 for information on reception window counters. 7
4.8 O-RU Adaptive Delay Capability 8
O-RUs may optionally support the ability to optimize their buffers based on information signalled concerning the configuration 9
of the O-DU, e.g., including the O-DU delay profile, together with transport delay information, which may have been derived 10
by the O-DU by using a delay measurement procedures operated by the O-DU or by other techniques.  This section describes 11
such optional O-RU buffer optimization functionality.  12
An O-RU that supports the optional adaptive timing capability shall indicate such to the O-RU Controller client by exchanging 13
NETCONF capabilities, as described in Section 6.2 and Annex C indicating that it supports the ADAPTIVE-O-RU-PROFILE 14
feature. An O-RU Controller may then provide the O-RU with the O-DU delay profile based on a combination of sub-carrier 15
spacing (SCS) and channel bandwidth, comprising the following parameters: 16
T1a_max_up: Corresponding to the earliest possible time which the O-DU can support transmitting an IQ data message 17
prior to transmission of the corresponding IQ samples at the antenna 18
TXmax: Corresponding to the maximum amount of time which the O-DU requires to transmit all downlink user plane IQ 19
data message for a symbol. 20
Ta4_max: Corresponding to the latest possible time which the O-DU can support receiving the last uplink user plane IQ 21
data message for a symbol 22
RXmax: Corresponding to the maximum time difference the O-DU can support between receiving the first user plane IQ 23
data message for a symbol and receiving the last user plane IQ data message for the same symbol. 24
T1a_max_cp_dl: Corresponding to the earliest possible time which the O -DU can support transmitting the downlink real 25
time control message prior to transmission of the corresponding IQ samples at the antenna. 26
In addition to the O-DU delay profile, the O-RU-Controller provides the O-RU with the transport network timing parameters: 27
T12_min: Corresponding to the minimum delay between any O-DU and O-RU processing elements 28
T12_max:  Corresponding to the maximum delay between O-DU and O-RU processing elements 29
T34_min: Corresponding to the minimum delay between any O-RU and O-DU processing elements 30
T34_max:  Corresponding to the maximum delay between O-RU and O-DU processing elements 31
The O-RU may use this information to adapt its delay profile, ensuring that the inequalities defined in Annex B of [2] are still 32
valid  33
The O-RU controller will typically provide this information during the O-RU’s start-up procedure. If an O-RU receives the 34
adaptive delay configuration information when operating a carrier, the O-RU shall not adapt its O-RU delay profile until all 35
carriers operating using the O-RU buffers have been disabled. Once an O-RU has adapted its O-RU profile, it will include the 36
newly adapted timing values when signaling its delay parameters to a NETCONF client. 37
4.9 Measuring transport delay parameters 38
An O-RU may optionally indicate that it supports the eCPRI based measurement of transport delays between O-DU and O-RU, 39
as described in [2].  40
When indicated that it supports the optional eCPRI based delay measurement, an O-RU shall support the processing of delay 41
measurement messages at any time, including whenever the C/U plane is configured. As well as the O-RU including its timing 42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          44
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
compensation values in the eCPRI delay measurement messages (tcv1 and tcv2 shown in the figure below), the YANG model 1
additionally enables a NETCONF client to recover these parameters from the O-RU over the M-Plane interface. 2
 3
Figure 11: eCPRI One-Way Delay Measurement procedure [2] 4
An O-RU that supports the eCPRI based delay measurement capability, shall be able to support simultaneous operation of delay 5
measurements over any processing element configured as described in section 4.5. For each processing element configured for 6
use by the del ay measurement procedure, the O-RU shall keep a record of the number of responses, requests and follow -up 7
messages transmitted by the O-RU. 8
4.10 O-RU Monitoring of C/U Plane Connectivity  9
The O-RU is responsible for monitoring the C/U plane connection and raising an alarm if the logical C/U -plane connection 10
associated with a processing -element fails. The O -RU uses a timer to monitor the C/U plane connection on a per processing -11
element basis. This timer is enabled only when at least one array-carrier using the processing-element is in the active state and 12
is reset whenever it receives any C/U plane data flows associated with the particular processing-element. Because of the variety 13
of PHY and C/U plane configurations, the O -RU cannot independently determine the minimum frequency of messages across 14
the fronthaul interface. Therefore, as a default, the O -RU shall use a timer value of 160 milliseconds for monitoring the C/U 15
plane connection. An O-RU may indicate that its C/U-plane monitoring timer is configurable, by the presence of the cu-plane-16
monitoring container in the o-ran-supervision.yang model. A NETCONF client can use the container to configure the O-RU’s 17
timer value, including being able to disable the operation of C/U Plane monitoring. 18
Note, if the O-RU supports this timer, then depending on how long the O-DU takes to initiate sending of C/U plane data 19
flows, it may be advisable for the NETCONF client to initially disable the operation of the timer before carrier activation. 20
Such an approach will avoid the O-RU sending spurious alarm notifications triggered by O-DU delays in initializing the 21
sending of C/U plane data that exceed the default timer value. Once C/U plane data flows have commenced, the NECTONF 22
client can re-configure the timer with the desired value and hence activate monitoring of the C/U plane connectivity by the O-23
RU. 24
 25

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          45
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
4.11 Bandwidth Management 1
An O-RU can indicate the maximum bitrate able to be supported on those interfaces associated with a particular physical port 2
using the optional nominal-bitrate leaf in the o -ran-transceiver YANG module. When the sustainable bitrate able to be 3
supported by an O -RU is less than the combined bitrates of all its physical ports, an O -RU can use the optional interface-4
grouping container in the o -ran-interfaces YANG model to define the maximum sustainable rate able to be supported by an 5
interface-group-id corresponding to a group of one or more physical interfaces. The same YANG model is used to augment 6
the ietf-interfaces defined interface list with the interface-group-id to which the interface belongs. 7
Note, the maximum sustainable bandwidth is calculated over one radio frame, meaning that the peak bandwidth can 8
exceed the defined value over time periods shorter than one radio frame. 9
Chapter 5 Software Management 10
The Software Management function provides a set of operations allowing the desired software build to be downloaded, installed 11
and activated at O-RU. Successful software activation operation does not mean an O-RU is running the just activated software 12
build. An O-RU reset RPC is required to trigger the O-RU to take the activated software build into operational use. 13
A single software build is considered as set of internally consistent files compliant within such a build. Replacement of files 14
within a build is prohibited, as this will cause software version incompatibility. Software build is a subject of versioning and 15
maintenance and as such cannot be broken. 16
The use of compression and ciphering for the content of the software build is left to vendor implementation. The only file which 17
shall never be ciphered is the manifest.xml file.  18
It is also Vendor's responsibility to handle SW Build / package / file integrity check. 19
The O-RU provides a set of so called "software slots" or "slots". Each slot provides an independent storage location for a single 20
software build. The number of slots offered by O-RU depends on the device’s capabilities. At least two writable slots shall be 21
available at the O-RU for failsafe update operation. Presence of read only slot is optional. The software slots are resources 22
provided by the O-RU and as such are not the subject of creation and deletion. The size of individual software slots is fixed and 23
determined by the O-RU's vendor and sufficient to accommodate the full software build. 24
Note: procedures used in Software Management are covered by o-ran.software-management.yang module. 25
5.1 Software Package 26
The software package is delivered by the O-RU vendor. 27
Each software package includes: 28
- manifest.xml 29
- software files to be installed on O-RU 30
 31
The name of package should follow the following format: 32
“<Vendor Code><Vendor Specific Field>[#NUMBER].EXT” 33
Where: 34
- Vendor Code is a mandatory part which has two capital characters, 35
- Vendor Specific Field is any set of characters allowed in filename. The value must not include character “_” (underscore) 36
or “#” (hash). The value can be defined per vendor for the human readable information. Version information is necessary 37
in the Vendor Specific Field which defines load version, 38
- NUMBER is optional and used when the original file is split into smaller pieces – number after “#” indicates the number 39
of a piece. Numbering starts from 1 and must be continuous, 40

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          46
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
- EXT is a mandatory part which defines the extension of filename. A vendor provides one or more software packages. Eack 1
software package shall be compressed by zip. 2
Note: the name of package needs a <Vendor Code> prefix to avoid issue if two vendors provide files with same name. 3
Note: the NETCONF client shall support ZIP functionality to enable support of compressed files types.  4
Note: the operator needs to manage and control which O-RU files will be stored and used in the file server, e.g., based on O-5
RU files provided by O-RU vendors and network configurations. The operator needs to make sure that only the expected version 6
of O-RU files will be transferred from the file server to the O-RU. Different versions of files for O-RU with the same vendor 7
and same product code should be avoided. 8
The content of the manifest.xml file allows to maintain software update process correctly in terms of compatibility between O-9
RU hardware and software build to be downloaded. The content of the Manifest file prohibits the O-RU from installing software 10
builds designed for device based on different hardware. The format of the manifest.xml file is: 11
<xml> 12
<manifest version=”1.0”> /// @version describes version of file format (not the content) 13
 <products> 14
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818820\.x11” name=”RUXX.x11” build-Id=”1”/>  15
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818820\.x12” name=”RUXX.x12” build-Id=”1”/> 16
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818818\…” name=”RUYY” build-Id=”2”/>  17
  /// @vendor is as reported by O-RU 18
  /// @code is a regular expression that is checked against productCode reported by O-RU 19
  /// @name is optional and used for human reading – MUST NOT be used for other purposes! 20
  /// @buildId is value of build@id (see below) 21
 </products> 22
 <builds> 23
  <build id=”1” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 24
  /// @id is index of available builds. 25
  /// @bldName and @bldVersion are used in YANG (build-name, build-version) 26
   <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 27
package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 28
   <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 29
package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 30
   /// @fileName and @fileVersion are used in YANG (name, version) 31
   /// @path is full path (with name and extension) of a physical file, relative to package 32
root folder,used in YANG (local-path) 33
   /// @checksum is used to chech file integrity on O-RU side 34
  </build> 35
  <build id=”2” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 36
   <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 37
package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 38
   <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 39
package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 40
   <file fileName=”zzzz” fileVersion=”1.5” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 41
package -root-folder” checksum=”ABCDEF”/ > 42
  </build> 43
 </builds> 44
</manifest> 45
</xml> 46
 47
Note: Keywords in manifest.xml example are in bold, the keywords must be strictly followed considering of cross-vendor cases. 48
Note 2: Correspondence between content of manifest.xml tags and content of o-ran-software-management.yang is: 49
- XML tag "product vendor" corresponds to content leaf "vendor-code", 50
- XML tag "code" corresponds to content of leaf "product-code", 51
- XML tag "build-Id" corresponds to content of leaf "build-id", 52
- XML tag "bldName" corresponds to content of leaf "build-name", 53
- XML tag "bldVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "build-version", 54
- XML tag "fileName" corresponds to content of leaf "name" in list "files", 55
-XML tag "fileVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "version" in list "files" 56

5.2 Software Inventory 1
Pre-condition:  2
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 3
Post-condition: 4
- NETCONF client successfully collected the software inventory information from NETCONF server. 5
 6
 7
Figure 12: Inventory fetch call flow 8
Software Inventory is fetched by a NETCONF Client using the NETCONF get rpc filtered over the software-slot container. 9
The response contains information about each software slot and its contents. 10
The following information is provided by software-inventory reply message: 11
a) name - name of the software slot (the name is defined by the O-RU vendor) 12
b) status - status of the software package. Status of the package can be  13
 - VALID - Slot contains a software build considered as proven valid. 14
 - INVALID - software build is not currently used by O-RU. The software is considered by the O-RU as damaged 15
(e.g. wrong CRC). 16
Activation of a software slot containing  an invalid software build shall be prohibited. Note: failed software install 17
operation can cause a slot status to change to "Invalid". 18
 - EMPTY - software slot does not contain a software package. Activation of an empty software slot shall be 19
prohibited.  20

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          48
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
c) active - indicates if the software stored in particular slot is activated at the moment. 1
 - True - software slot contains an activated software build. Active::True can be assigned only for slots with status 2
"Valid". At any time, only one slot in the O-RU MUST be marked as Active::True. The O-RU shall reject activation 3
for software slots with status "Empty" and "Invalid". 4
 - False - software slot contains passive software build or is empty 5
d) running - informs if software stored in particular slot is used at the moment. 6
 - True - software slot contains the software build used by the O-RU in its current run. 7
 - False - software slot contains a software build not used by O-RU at the moment. 8
e) access – informs about access rights for the current slot 9
- READ_ONLY – The slot is intended only for factory software, activation of such software slot means performing 10
a factory reset operation and a return to factory defaults settings. 11
- READ_WRITE – slot used for updating software 12
f) product-code - product code provided by the vendor, specific to the product. 13
g) vendor-code - unique code of the vendor. 14
h) build-id - Identity associated with the software build.  This id is used to find the appropriate build -version for the 15
product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 16
i) build-name - Name of the software build. 17
j) build-version - Version of the software build for the product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 18
k) files – list of files in build 19
l) name – name of one particular file 20
m) version – version of the file 21
n) local-path - complete path of the file on local file system 22
o) integrity - result of the file integrity check 23
- OK – file integrity is correct 24
- NOK – file is corrupted 25
If a slot contains a file with integrity::NOK, the O-RU shall mark the whole slot with status::INVAL ID. The content of a 26
software-slot is fully under O-RU's management - including removal of the content occupying the slot (in case the slot is subject 27
of software update procedure), control of file system consistency and so on. The slot content shall not be removed until there is 28
a need for new software to be installed.  29
Note: The empty slot parameters shall be as follows 30
name: up to vendor, not empty 31
status: "INVALID" 32
active: False 33
running: False 34
access: READ_WRITE 35
product-code: up to vendor 36
vendor code: up to vendor 37

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          49
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
build-name: null (empty string) 1
build-version: null (empty string) 2
files: empty 3
5.3 Download 4
Pre-condition:  5
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 6
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive download-event notifications. 7
Post-condition: 8
- O-RU downloads all files specified and successfully stores the downloaded files in the O-RU’s file system.  9

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          50
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 1
 2
Figure 13: Software download call flow 3
Following types of authentications are supported for software-download: 4
a) password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 5
b) certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 6
The software-download rpc is used to trigger the downloading of software to the O-RU. The download shall be performed 7
using sFTP. The rpc specifies the URI of the remote location of the software files.  8
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 9
a) STARTED – software download operation has been started 10
b) FAILED – software download operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message  11

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          51
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
When the O-RU completes the software download or software download fail s, the O-RU shall send NETCONF download-1
event notification with one of the following statuses: 2
a) COMPLETED 3
b) AUTHENTICATION_ERROR -  source available, wrong credentials 4
c) PROTOCOL_ERROR – sFTP protocol error 5
d) FILE_NOT_FOUND -  source not available 6
e) APPLICATION_ERROR - operation failed due to internal reason  7
f) TIMEOUT -  source available, credentials OK, Operation timed out  (e.g. source becomes unavailable during ongoing 8
operation). 9
The above will be repeated until all files which are required for the O-RU and which belong to the software package have been 10
downloaded to the O-RU. 11
5.4 Install 12
Pre-condition:  13
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 14
- At least one software slot with status active::False and running::False exists in O-RU. 15
- Software Download has been completed successfully and files are available in O-RU. 16
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive install-event notifications. 17
Post-condition: 18
- O-RU software is installed in the specified target software-slot. 19

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          52
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 1
 2
Figure 14 Software install call flow 3
NETCONF software-install rpc is used to install the previously downloaded software (all files provided in the package) to the 4
specified target software-slot on O-RU. This slot must have status active::False and running::False.  5
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 6
a) STARTED – software install operation has been started. 7
b) FAILED – software install operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message. 8
When O-RU completes the software install or software install procedure fails, the O-RU will send NETCONF install-event 9
notification with one of the following statuses: 10
a) COMPLETED - Install procedure is successfully completed. 11
b) FILE_ERROR – operation on the file resulted in in error, disk failure, not enough disk space, incompatible file format 12

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          53
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
c) INTEGRITY_ERROR – file is corrupted  1
d) APPLICATION_ERROR – operation failed due to internal reason 2
When the software install commences, the O-RU shall set the slot status to INVALID. After the install procedure finishes, the 3
O-RU shall change the slot status to its appropriate status. This operation avoids reporting of inaccurate status when the install 4
procedure is in operation or when it is interrupted (e.g., by spurious reset operation). 5
5.5 Activation 6
Pre-condition:  7
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 8
- Software slot to be activated has status VALID. 9
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive activation-event notifications. 10
Post-condition: 11
- O-RU software activates to the version of software-slot. 12
 13

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          54
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 1
 2
Figure 15 Software activation call flow. 3
NETCONF software-activate rpc is used to activate the software. The name of the software -slot is specified in the activate 4
request.  5

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          55
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 1
a) STARTED – software activation operation has been started 2
b) FAILED – software activation operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message 3
 4
When the activation is completed , the O-RU shall send the NETCONF activation-event notification with the status  of 5
activation. The following status is returned in the NETCONF activation-event notifications. 6
a) COMPLETED - Activation procedure is successfully completed. O-RU must be restarted via NETCONF reset rpc for the 7
new software to be activated. 8
b) APPLICATION_ERROR - operation failed due to internal reason 9
Only one software slot can be active at a ny time. Thus, successful software-activate command will set active::True to the slot 10
that was provided in the rpc and automatically will set active::False to the previously active slot. 11
NETCONF reset rpc shall be sent to O-RU to activate to the version of the software -slot. O-RU restarts and performs startup 12
procedure as described in Chapter 3 as regular startup with new software version running.  13
5.6 Software update scenario 14
An example scenario of a successful software update procedure can be as follows: 15
1. NETCONF client performs a software inventory operation and determines that a new software package is available 16
and can be installed on the O-RU 17
2. NETCONF client using the software-download rpc requests the O-RU to download a software package (if the 18
software package contains several files, steps 2-4 need to be performed repeatedly until all files have been downloaded) 19
3. O-RU sends rpc response that download was started 20
4. O-RU finishes downloading the file(s) and reports this by sending the download-event notification 21
5. NETCONF client requests installation of the software using software-install rpc, and provides the slot name where 22
the software needs to be installed along with a list of filenames to be installed (if the software package contains only 23
one file, the list will contain only one entry) 24
6. O-RU sends rpc response that installation was started 25
7. O-RU sets installation slot status to INVALID 26
8. O-RU installs the software and after successful install ation (with checksum control) change s status of the slot to 27
VALID 28
9. O-RU notifies the NETCONF client that the installation is finished using install-event notification 29
10. NETCONF client requests the O-RU to activate the newly installed software using the software-activate rpc 30
11. O-RU sends rpc response that activation was started 31
12. For requested slot, O-RU changes active to True and at the same time sets activate to False on previously active slot 32
13. O-RU notifies NETCONF client about activation finished using the activation-event notification 33
14. NETCONF client restarts the O-RU forcing it to use the newly installed and activated software into use. O-RU restarts 34
as regular startup with new software version running. 35

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          56
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
5.7 Factory Reset  1
O-RU can be reset to the factory default software by activat ing the software -slot containing the factory default software and 2
initiating NETCONF reset rpc. O-RU may clear persistent memory data during factory reset as vendor implementation option. 3
Chapter 6 Configuration Management  4
6.1 Baseline configuration 5
This chapter describes NETCONF standard operation (edit-config/get-config/get) [3] which belongs to the CM in Module  to 6
modify/retrieve any parameters in YANG modules. Examples below use o-ran-hardware as an example YANG module. 7
Two following scenarios are feasible for Configuration Management purposes. 8
- 2 phase (modify/commit) operation using writable running datastore 9
- 3 phase (modify/commit/confirm) operation using candidate datastore. 10
The 2-phase operation performs edit config on running datastore directly and confirm operation is not used. 11
All O-RUs shall support 2 phase operation, with 3 phase operations being optional. 12
6.1.1 Retrieve State 13
O-RU Controller is able to retrieve state which is defined in o-ran-hardware by using NETCONF <get> procedure: 14
 15
 16
 Figure 16 – Retrieve Resource State 17
Preconditions: 18
- O-RU Controller has completed exchange of NETCONF capabilities as part of connection establishment between O-RU and 19
O-RU Controllers. 20
Post conditions: 21
- O-RU controller has retrieved O-RU state as per <get> request.  22
6.1.2 Modify State 23
O-RU Controller is able to change state which can be configurable by using NETCONF <edit-config> procedure without reset. 24

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          57
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
The configurable state are admin-state and power-state defined in o-ran-hardware. 1
In case of a failure, an error will be returned. Please refer to RFC6241 Appendix A for error codes. 2
The vendor can define the behavior after the error occurred. 3
 4
 5

6.1.3 Retrieve Parameters 23

6.1.4 Modify Parameters 10
Before an O -RU Controller modifies the configuration (candidate or running) of an O -RU, it shall first lock the target 11
configuration. This prevents other NETCONF clients from changing the shared configuration database until the O -RU 12
Controller releases the lock. If another NETCONF client has already locked the configuration datastore, then the O -RU will 13
respond with a NETCONF error indicating that the requested lock is denied. Note, in such circumstances, the O-RU controller 14
should wait for a period of time before re-attempting to modify the O-RU’s configuration. 15
O-RU Controller is able to modify parameters of the YANG module by using the NETCONF <edit-config> procedure. 16
Note, validation of the modified configuration is based on: 17
1) basic YANG constraints (e.g., min-elements, range, pattern),  18
2) XPATH based YANG constraints (e.g., leafref, must and when statements), and  19
3) external code which implements YANG constraints (e.g., defined in O -RAN specifications, YANG description 20
statements, etc.). 21
In case of failures, an error will be returned. Please refer to RFC6241 Appendix A for error codes. 22
The vendor can define the behavior after error occurred. 23

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          61
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 1
 2
Figure 25 – Modify Parameters 3
Preconditions: 4
- O-RU Controller has completed exchange of NETCONF capabilities as part of connection establishment between the O-RU 5
and O-RU Controller(s). 6
- O-RU Controller has locked the target configuration 7
Post conditions: 8
- O-RU controller has retrieved O-RU resource state as per <edit-config> request 9
• Success case: The update is confirmed to O-RU Controller. 10
• Failure case: Failure reason is provided to O-RU Controller 11
Sequential processing is assumed.  Only a single <edit -config> rpc is allowed at a time. Next <edit -config> rpc shall be 12
performed after previous <edit-config> rpc reply. 13
Modify Parameters is used to:  14
- update parameters of existing leafs,  15
O-RU shall be allowed to reject <edit -config> in case the content is found to be against e.g. , functions supported by O-RU - 16
like carrier configured out of band. 17
After the modification procedure is complete, the O-RU Controller releases the lock on the target configuration. 18
6.2 Framework for optional feature handling 19
This section describes the common and optional features about Configuration Management. 20

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          62
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
An O-RU may have some features which are not supported by other O-RUs, i.e. optional feature (s). In this case, the O-RU 1
needs to inform the O-RU controller which features the O-RU can provide, and this can be achieved by exchanging NETCONF 2
capabilities. 3
Some of the YANG mo dels are optional for the O-RU to support. For example, in this version of the management plane 4
specification, those models associated with External IO and Antenna Line Devices are not essential for the operation of the O-5
RAN fronthaul interface. Other mandatory models define optional feature capabilities. 6
The NETCONF Server shall use the ietf-yang-library model (RFC 7895) [20] to list the namespace of the models supported by 7
the Server. If an O-RU/NETCONF server does not return the namespace assoc iated with an optional YANG model, the 8
NETCONF client determines that the O-RU does not support the optional capability associated with the model. 9
In addition, for each supported schema, the ietf-yang-library lists the YANG feature names from this module that are supported 10
by the server. The details of optional models and features are defined in Annex C. 11
6.3 M-Plane Operational State 12
The o-ran-mplane-int YANG model allows the O-RU to report the connectivity to NETCONF clients on a per sub -interface 13
level. The client information includes the IP address(es) for the client(s) as well as the link-layer address used to forward packets 14
towards the various management plane clients. 15
6.4 Notification of Updates to Configuration Datastore 16
6.4.1 Introduction 17
This sub-section defines an optional O-RU capability which allows O-RU Controllers to configure the O-RU to provide 18
notifications of modifications to its YANG datastore. This capability can be used when the O-RU is operating in a hybrid 19
environment with multiple simultaneous NETCONF sessions established to different O-RU controllers. Using this capability, 20
one particular O-RU controller uses the NETCONF notifications functionality specified in RFC 6470 [35] to enable it to be 21
automatically signalled changes to the O-RU’s configuration made by a second O-RU controller. Additionally, if the O-RU 22
supports a vendor specific interface to allow manual configuration, this functionality can also be used to signal such 23
configuration modifications to an O-RU Controller. 24
6.4.2 Subscribing to updates from an O-RU 25
When an O-DU receives an indication from an O-RU that it supports the optional capability to support notification of updates 26
to its configuration data store, as a minimum, it shall subscribe to the netconf-config-change notification. 27
An example subscription to the event notification stream is shown in Figure 26, where one O-RU Controller is receiving a 28
notification that the configuration of the O-RU’s timezone offset has been modified by a second O-RU controller.  29

Chapter 7 Performance Management 4
This chapter provides the description of scenarios related to performance management. It consists of 2 functions. One is for the 5
measurement activation and the other is the collection of measurement results. 6
7.1 Measurement Activation and De-activation 7
The measurement activation at the start-up installation is also allowed as described in chapter 3.  8
Pre-condition:  9
M-Plane is operational.  10
Post-condition: 11
Measurement is activated or deactivated as per NETCONF client’s request. 12
This sub -section provides information about how to activate  and de-activate the performance measurement via NETCONF 13
<edit-config> to O-RU. The performance measurement is defined as o-ran-performance-management YANG module. In case 14
of multiple NETCONF clients, only one NETCONF client shall activate/deactivate the measurements in the O-RU. 15
In the performance-management YANG module, the following parameters are defined. 16
- group of the measurement results, e.g., transceiver-measurement-objects, rx-window-measurement-objects, tx-17
measurement-objects and epe-measurement-objects. 18
- measurement-interval: measurement interval for the measurement-objects to measure the performance periodically, 19
e.g., 300, 600, 900 seconds. It is defined per the group of the measurement result. 20
- measurement-object: target metric to measure the performance, e.g., RX_POWER, TX_POWER , defined  as key 21
parameter. 22
- active: enable/disable the performance measurement per measurement-object. This va lue is Boolean.  Default is 23
FALSE. 24
- start-time and end-time: to report the time of measurement start and end for the measurement-object at each 25
measurement-interval. 26
- object-unit: unit to measure the performance per object, e.g., O-RU, physical port number, antenna, carrier. The object-27
unit may be configurable  Identifier object-unit-id means e.g., physical port number when object unit set to physical 28
port number. 29
<notification xmlns="urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:netconf:notification:1.0">
  <eventTime>2020-03-01T08:00:14.12Z</eventTime>
  <netconf-config-change xmlns= "urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:yang:ietf-netconf-
notifications">
    <id>102</id>
    <changed-by>
      <username>nms-user</username>
      <session-id>1099</session-id>
      <source-host>10.10.10.10</source-host>
    </changed-by>
    <datastore>running</datastore>
    <edit>
      <target>/oran-ops:operational-info/oran-ops:clock/oran-
ops:timezoneutc-offset</target>
      <operation>replace</operation>
    </edit>
  </netconf-config-change>
</notification>

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          64
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
- report-info: th e reporting info to the measurement-object, e.g., MAXIMUM, MINIMUM, FIRST, LATEST, 1
FREQUENCY_TABLE and COUNT. Multiple info can be considered for one object if necessary. 2
- Optional configurable parameter(s) for report-info: some configurable parameters to report, e.g., function, bin-count, 3
upper-bound, lower-bound. For the bin-count configuration, it shall be less than the parameter max-bin-count that is 4
the capability information of NETCONF server for the maximum configurable value for bin-count. 5
- Additional reporting information for report-info: some additional information to report info, e.g., date-and-time. 6
 7
The detail of the parameters per measurement-object and the group of measurement result are defined in Annex B. 8
The measurement-interval of measurement-object may be set to common or different values per group of the measurement 9
result.  10
It is allowed that the measurement is activated and deactivated at any time. When different parameter measurements have 11
intervals with a common factor, the O-RU shall synchronize the boundary of these measurements aligned with this factor, 12
irrespective of when the different measurements are activated. And all of start point s of the measurement-intervals shall be 13
synchronized to zero o’clock mid-night by using an equation {full seconds (hour, minute and second) modulo ‘measurement-14
interval’ = 0}, in order to ensure the same start and end of the measurement-intervals between O-RUs. For more detail see 15
the following illustration. 16
 17
Figure 27: synchronization of measurement-interval. 18
 19
The modification of the configurable parameters for the measurement shall be allowed  while active for the corresponding 20
measurement-object is set to FALSE. 21
All of the measurements are optionally supported in the O-RU.  22
The report-info, e.g., count, shall be started from 0 at the boundary of every measurement-interval. No accumulation is 23
applied between the measurement-intervals. 24
 7.2 Collection and Reporting of Measurement Result 25
This sub-section provides the description of scenarios used to collect measurement results. There are three options. 26
1. NETCONF process: Create-subscription from NETCONF client and NETCONF notification from NETCONF server 27
are used. 28
2. File Management process: File upload mechanism is used for the measurement file from O-RU to configured file 29
server(s) that O-RU can reach to. 30
3. Configured subscription process: Create configured subscription from O-RU as Event-Producer to Event-Collector. 31

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          65
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
Methods 1 and 2 are mandatory for the O-RU. Method 3 shall be supported by those O -RUs that support the optional NON-1
PERSISTENT-MPLANE feature. The method(s) to be used is the matter of NETCONF client. 2
In case of multiple NETCONF clients and/or Event-Collectors, the O-RU shall report the same notification-based measurement 3
results to all subscribed NETCONF clients /Event-Collectors, and the O-RU shall upload file-based results to all configured 4
fileservers. 5
7.2.1 NETCONF process 6
This process needs the NETCONF capability: urn:ietf:params:netconf:capability:notification:1.0 7
1. NETCONF client subscribes to one or more measurement  group(s) and/or measurement-object(s) to collect the 8
measurement result by sending NETCONF <subscribe-notification> to NETCONF server in the O-RU. In this message, 9
startTime and stopTime for the notification may be configurable. NETCONF client can configure the notification-interval 10
in the performance-measurement YANG module.  11
2.  NETCONF server sends NETCONF notifica tion messages periodically to the client as configured by  the notification-12
interval. The NETCONF notification message contains subscribed measurement group(s) and/or measurement-object(s). 13
The notification-interval doesn’t need to be same as the measurement-interval. The notification timing different from the 14
measurement-interval is a matter to O-RU implementation. 15
This procedure is described in the following figure. 16
 17
Figure 28: NETCONF process of Measurement Result Collection 18
Note: This figure uses create-subscription for the single stream " measurement-result-stats". In order to subscribe multiple 19
notifications, the appropriate create-subscription message is required. Please refer to section 8.2 for the appropriate example 20
of create-subscription of multiple notifications. 21
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall send <close-session> operation from the subscription session. 22
If NETCONF session is terminated by <kill-session>, the subscribed notification is terminated as well.  23
This procedure is described in the following figure. 24

When notification-interval is larger than measurement-interval, one notification may contain multiple stats which have 3
consecutive periods indicating start-time and end-time for the measurement. 4
When notification-interval is smaller than measurement-interval, one notification may not contain the stats which start-time 5
and end-time are not applicable to the period for the notification. 6
For example, when notification-interval = 60min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 7
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one n otification contains 2 measurement results for 8
measurement-object#A with consecutive start-time and end-time, and 4 measurement results for measurement-object#B 9
with consecutive start-time and end-time.  10
For the other example, when notification-interval = 15min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 11
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one notification contains one measurement results for 12
measurement-object#B but not for measurement-object#A. next notification contains b oth measurements result for 13
measurement-object#A and #B. 14

7.2.2 File Management process 16
NETCONF client needs to configure a parameter of performance measurement YANG module ‘enable-SFTP-upload’ to 17
enable or disable the periodic file upload mechanism via NETCONF <edit-config>. Its default is FALSE. 18
In addition, t he performance measurement YANG module defines file-upload-interval, remote-SFTP-upload-path, 19
credentials information of the file server and enable-random-file-upload as configurable parameters. 20
Following types of authentications are supported for performance file upload: 21
a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 22
b) Certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 23
When the parameter enable-SFTP-upload is set to TRUE, O-RU shall store the performance measurement files in the generic 24
folder in O-RU, i.e., O-RAN/PM/. Every file-upload-interval, O-RU pushes the latest file to upload to the  remote-SFTP-25
upload-path of the configured SFTP servers if enable-SFTP-upload is set to TRUE. Otherwise, the performance measurement 26
file is not created and uploaded. The number of maximum performance files to be stored in O-RU simultaneously is a matter 27
for O-RU implementation. The O-RU shall manage its own storage space by deleting the older files autonomously.  28

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          67
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
The O-RU shall ensure that the start-time and the  end-time within the name of the performance measurement file are 1
synchronized with the same manner as measurement-interval by using file-upload-interval. 2
If the parameter enable-random-file-upload is set to TRUE, the O-RU shall randomize the timing to upload SFTP file after 3
the performance measurement file is ready to upload. The randomized timing is an O-RU implementation matter and shall not 4
be later than next file-upload-interval. 5
The file name of the performance measurement is: 6
C<start-time>_<end-time>_<name>.csv 7
- Starting with a capital letter “C”. 8
- Format of <start-time> and <end-time> can be local time or UTC. 9
Local time format is YYYYMMDDHHMM+HHMM, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute, timezone “+” or “ -“, 10
hour and minute for the time zone. 11
UTC format is YYYYMMDDHHMMZ, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute and with a special UTC designator 12
("Z")   13
Time zone offset is provided by timezone-utc-offset in o-ran-operation.yang. 14
- <name> in ietf-hardware is used  15
- “_” underscore is located between <start-time>, <end-time> and <name> 16
- File extension is “csv” as csv format file. 17
Example of measurement file is: 18
C201805181300+0900_201805181330+0900_ABC0123456.csv. 19
 20
The file format of the performance measurement has following rule: 21
1. Each line starts with the measurement-object identifier, which measurement can be switched to TRUE or FALSE by 22
active parameter. The identifier of each measurement-object is defined in Annex B. 23
2. After the measurement-object identifier, the name of measurement-object, start-time, end-time are followed. 24
3. Since the report-info results of any measurement-object are measured per object-unit, object-unit-id and set of report-25
info are repeated in one line. 26
4. When multiple report-info parameters exist per object-unit, all of the report-info are consecutively listed until the next 27
object-unit-id. The order of parameters, such as objec t-unit-id, report-info and additional information for the report-info, 28
shall be same as the order of those listed in NETCONF notification defined in o-ran-performance-management YANG 29
module. 30
Example of measurement result in one line is: 31
1, RX_ON_TIME, 2018-05-18T13:00:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00, 0, 123, AAAA , 1, 123, BBBB, 2, 123, CCCC, 3, 123, 32
DDDD 33

- EAXC_ID: 0 38

7.2.3 Configured Subscription Process 34
This optional process requires the O-RU to support configured subscriptions, as described in Chapter 15. The structure of the 35
process follows the NETCONF process described in sub -section 7.2.1. However, instead of sending a NETCONF <create -36
subscription > to the NETCONF server in the O-RU to subscribe to the measurement-result-stats notifications, the NETCONF 37
client installs the subscription via configuration of the O -RU’s datastore. Based on configured subscriptions, the O-RU sends 38
asynchronous YANG notifications over HTTPS to the configured Event-Collector. 39
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall delete the corresponding configuration in the O -RU. 40
Immediately after the subscription is successfully deleted, the O -RU will send to a subscription state change notification 41
indicating that the subscription has ended to the Event-Collector.  42

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          69
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
Note, unlike the NETCONF process described in section 7.2.1, the subscription to the subscribed notifications is not terminated 1
when the NETCONF session used to establish the subscription is terminated.  2
Chapter 8 Fault Management 3
Fault management is responsible for sending alar m notifications to the configured subscriber, which will typically be the 4
NETCONF Client  unless the O -RU supports the configured subscription capability, as described in Chapter 15, when the 5
configured subscriber may be an Event-Collector. FM contains Faul t Management Managed Element and via this Managed 6
Element alarm notifications can be disabled or enabled. 7
The NETCONF Server is responsible for managing an “active -alarm-list”. Alarms with severity “warning” are excluded from 8
this list. When an alarm is detected it is added to the list; when the alarm reason disappears then the alarm is cleared - removed 9
from the “active-alarm-list”. Furthermore, when the element that was the “fault -source” of an alarm is deleted then all related 10
alarms are removed from the “active-alarm-list”. 11
The NETCONF Client can read “active-alarm-list” by get rpc operation. 12
 13
Figure 30: Read Active Alarms 14
8.1 Alarm Notification 15
The O-RU is responsible to send <alarm -notif> to a configured subscriber  when the NETCONF Client has established a 16
subscription to alarm notification and: 17
- a new alarm is detected (this can be the same alarm as an already existing one, but reported against a different “fault-source” 18
than the existing alarm)  19
- an alarm is removed from the list   20
Removal of alarms from the list due to deletion of “fault-source” element is considered as clearing and cause sending of <alarm-21
notif> to the configured subscriber. This applies to alarms which were explicitly related to the deleted “fault -source” element. 22
The rationale for such is to avoid misalignment between NETCONF Clients when one NETCONF Client deletes an element.  23
The O-RU reports in <alarm-notif> only for new active or cancelled alarms, not all active alarms. 24

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          70
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
 1
Figure 31: Alarm Notification 2
8.2 Manage Alarms Request to NETCONF Clients 3
The NETCONF Client can “subscribe” to Fault Management Element by sending create-subscription, RFC5277 [21], to 4
NETCONF Server. 5
RFC5277 allows <create-subscription> below: 6
        <netconf:rpc netconf:message-id="101" 7
                xmlns:netconf="urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:netconf:base:1.0"> 8
          <create-subscription 9
              xmlns="urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:netconf:notification:1.0"> 10
            <filter netconf:type="subtree"> 11
              <event xmlns="http://example.com/event/1.0"> 12
                <eventClass>fault</eventClass> 13
                <severity>critical</severity> 14
              </event> 15
              <event xmlns="http://example.com/event/1.0"> 16
                <eventClass>fault</eventClass> 17
                <severity>major</severity> 18
              </event> 19
              <event xmlns="http://example.com/event/1.0"> 20
                <eventClass>fault</eventClass> 21
                <severity>minor</severity> 22

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          71
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
              </event> 1
            </filter> 2
          </create-subscription> 3
        </netconf:rpc> 4
Note: the NETCONF Client can disable/enable alarm sending only for all the alarms with same severity, not for single alarms. 5

8.3 Fault Sources 8
Alarm notifications reported by NETCONF Server contain element “fault -source” which indicates the origin of an alarm. In 9
general values of “fault-source” are based on names defined as YANG leafs: 10
- Source (Examples: fan, module, PA, port) 11

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          73
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
indicates that origin of the alarm within the O-RU. Value of “fault-source” is based on element name. 1
Note: In case the NETCONF Server reports an unknown “fault-source”, the NETCONF Client can discard the <alarm-2
notif>. 3
- Source (other than when an element is within the O-RU) 4
Value of fault-source may be empty or may identify the most likely external candidate; for example, antenna line.   5
 6
Alarms with different “fault-id”, “fault-source” or "fault-severity" are independent: 7
- Multiple alarms with same “fault-id” may be reported with different “fault-source”.  8
- Multiple alarms with same “fault-source” may be reported with different “fault-id”.  9
- When an alarm with a "fault -id" and a "fault-source" is reported with a "fault -severity" and its severity of alarm condition 10
is upgraded or degraded, NETCONF ser ver reports a new alarm with the same "fault -id" and the same "fault-source" with 11
the upgraded or degraded "fault -severity" with "is -cleared"::FALSE and clears the previous alarm with the report of the 12
"fault-id", "fault-source" and "fault-severity" with "is-cleared":: TRUE.  13
The range of "fault-id" is separated to common and vendor specific. The common fault -ids are defined in Annex A and more 14
number will be used in future. The vendor specific range for the fault-id shall be [1000 .. 65535]. 15
Alarm notifications reported by the NETCONF Server contain names of the “affected-objects” which indicate elements affected 16
by the fault. In case the origin of the alarm is within the O-RU, other elements than “fault-source” which will not work correctly 17
due to the alarm are reported via “affected -objects”. In case the origin of the fault is outside of the O-RU, the O-RU elements 18
which will not work correctly due to the fault are reported via “affected-objects”. 19
8.4 Manage Alarms Request to Event-Collector 20
This optional capability requires the O-RU to support configured subscriptions, as described in Chapter 15. The structure of the 21
process follows the process described in sub -section 8.2. However, instead of sending a NETCONF <create -subscription> to 22
the NETCONF server in the O-RU to subscribe to the alarm-notif notifications, the NETCONF client installs the subscription 23
via configuration of the O -RU’s datastore. Based on configured subscriptions, the O-RU sends asynchronous YANG 24
notifications over HTTPS to the configured Event-Collector. 25
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall delete the correspon ding configuration in the O -RU. 26
Immediately after the subscription is successfully deleted, the O -RU will send to a subscription state change notification 27
indicating that the subscription has ended to the Event-Collector.  28
Chapter 9 File Management 29
This chapter specifies File Management for the O-RU. Following operations are supported as a File Management. 30
- upload (see subsection 9.2) 31
 File upload from O-RU to file server triggered by O-RU Controller. 32
- retrieve file list (see subsection 9.3) 33
 O-RU Controller retrieves the file list in O-RU. 34
- download (see subsection 9.4) 35
 File download from file server to O-RU triggered by O-RU Controller 36
Note: file-download has different purpose with software-download specified in subsection 5.3. For example, file-download 37
can be used for Beamforming configuration in subsection 12.4. 38
File transfers are done with sFTP. Following types of authentications are supported for file management: 39

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          74
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 1
b) Certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 2
Following other sections are related with File Management. 3
- Subsection 7.2.2: File Management process (can be used for on demand file upload purpose, since subsection 7.2.2 covers 4
periodic file upload) 5
- Subsection 11.2: Log Management 6
- Subsection 12.4: Beamforming Configuration 7
9.1 File System Structure 8
The file System structure of the O-RU is represented as a logical structure that is used by the file management procedures 9
defined in the rest of this chapter. If the O-RU’s physical file structure differs from the logical file structure defined below, the 10
O-RU is responsible for performing the mapping between the two structures. 11
The O-RU shall support the standardized logical folders. In this version of the M-Plane specification, the following standardized 12
folders are defined: 13
O-RAN/log/ 14
O-RAN/PM/ 15
O-RAN/transceiver/ 16
And for those O-RU’s supporting beamforming 17
O-RAN/beamforming/ 18
The O-RU may additionally support vendor defined folders which are out of scope of this specification. 19
9.2 File Management Operation: upload 20
This subsection describes file upload method from O-RU to the fileserver. sFTP is used for File management, and one file can 21
be uploaded by one upload operation. The O-RU Controller triggers file upload operation to O-RU. 22
Simultaneous multiple file upload operations can be supported under the same sFTP connection between O-RU to the fileserver. 23
If the O-RU has the number of limitation to upload simultaneously as a capability, it is allowed that O-RU reports failure 24
notification for the upload request which is larger than the capability. The behaviour of O-RU Controller is out of scope when 25
O-RU Controller receives failure notification from the O-RU. 26
Following rpc is used for upload operation. 27
-rpc: file-upload 28
-  input 29
-  local-logical-file-path: the logical path of file to be uploaded (no wildcard is allowed) 30
-  remote-file-path: URI of file on the fileserver 31
-  output 32
-  status: whether O-RU accepted or rejected the upload request  33
-  reject-reason: the human readable reason why O-RU rejects the request (only applicable if status is rejected) 34
In the rpc-reply, status whether the O-RU receives the upload request or rejects due to some reason (e.g., the number of 35
limitation to upload simultaneously) is replied. If rejected, the human readable reject reason is also replied. 36

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          75
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v05.00
In notification, the result of the upload process (successfully uploaded or failed upload) is replied in addition to local -logical-1
file-path and remote-file-path. If failure, the human readable reason is also replied. 2
